{{rfcquote|text=
The primary argument here for noninclusion has appeared to be that such mentions by the blp's subject, found accompanying political commentary published at partisan opinion platforms (Breitbart, FNC, TheBlaze, the conservative imprint at Penguin Books, her own web platforms such as on Twitter), render such sourcing [[wp:BIASED]], therefore no such sourcing ought be resorted to within a blp. The primary argument pro-inclusion has seemed to be that, despite considerations of partisan media, within the spirit of [[wp:SELFPUB]], a subject is a reliable source about herself.--07:07, 28 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:List of Trump–Russia dossier allegations#rfc_ABDF2E8|Talk:List of Trump–Russia dossier allegations]] expired 2018-03-02 14:01 ===
* Id: ABDF2E8
* Date: 2018-02-10 17:35:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|824968069|POL 824968069}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|828429447|POL 828429447}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
'''Merge This article &rarr; [[Trump–Russia dossier]]'''

This article doesn't really have a good reason to stand alone other than length, and length is a problem that can be addressed with formatting and proper prose integration. If we merged this article into [[Trump–Russia dossier|the main article]], we could trim out all but the dry text outlining the allegation (a step that would, I believe, address many of the NPOV complaints made here), leaving the commentary to the main parts of the article. This could be formatted in a number of ways that would not make that article over-long. Indeed, much of the dry text describing the allegations could be trimmed significantly, as the details will have been given in the main body already. I mean, this article is about ''the contents'' of the dossier. I don't see any need to fork that off from the main article. <span style="text-shadow:grey 0.118em 0.118em 0.118em; class=texhtml">[[User:MjolnirPants|<font color="green">'''ᛗᛁᛟᛚᚾᛁᚱPants'''</font>]] [[User_talk:MjolnirPants|<small>Tell me all about it.</small>]]</span> 17:35, 10 February 2018 (UTC)}}

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|824186869|POL 824186869}}

{{rfcquote|text=

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Film#rfc_81F0AE4|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Film]] expired 2018-03-03 23:01 ===
* Id: 81F0AE4
* User: Hoverfish
* Date: 2018-03-01 14:27:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|828264326|MEDIA 828264326}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|833436158|MEDIA 833436158}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Since last year, [[User:‎Michael 182]], also as [[User:TwentySteps]] (blocked) and via various IP edits (some blocked for socking), has been splitting several film award articles that were previously arranged in one whole table, most of them sortable, into tables by decades. Venice Festival awards: [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Golden_Lion&type=revision&diff=808058639&oldid=806091076], [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Silver_Lion&type=revision&diff=808062802&oldid=799768892], [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Volpi_Cup_for_Best_Actor&type=revision&diff=808066192&oldid=803129364], [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Volpi_Cup_for_Best_Actress&type=revision&diff=808099890&oldid=803130412]. Berlin Festival awards: [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Golden_Bear&type=revision&diff=807743545&oldid=800928169], [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Silver_Bear_for_Best_Director&type=revision&diff=807958060&oldid=800929501], [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Silver_Bear_for_Best_Actor&type=revision&diff=807960820&oldid=801812885], [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Silver_Bear_for_Best_Actress&type=revision&diff=808049871&oldid=801819695]. He has also done various changes in Academy Awards and Primetime Emmy Awards which are outside of my scope of interest in films. Note also that I have not opposed the division by decades in director and actor awards as this is also outside my focus of interest, plus I find no meaningful sortability damaged in so splitting them.

From several discussions I have participated or just followed in WP:Film, I am aware that by longstanding consensus the preferred format for presenting film award lists, is by using one stortable table. Splitting such a table to smaller tables by decades (sortable or not) disables any meaningful sortability throughout the whole list. If split by decades, one cannot get either a full alphabetical list of Directors or of Films that won a certain award any longer. Since the user claims that there is not sufficient evidence that such consensus exists, I am doing here a formal RfC to have some consensus on this issue clearly found in one place, also for future reference. 1. Should the film award articles be kept in one sortable table or split in decades? 2. Should director and actress/actor awards be kept in one sortable table or split in decades? [[User:Hoverfish|Hoverfish]] <small>[[User talk:Hoverfish|Talk]]</small> 14:27, 1 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Did you know#rfc_8644A56|Wikipedia talk:Did you know]] expired 2018-03-04 02:01 ===
* Id: 8644A56
* User: Vanamonde93
* Date: 2018-02-11 17:27:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|825132945|POLICY 825132945}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|828676913|POLICY 828676913}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The role of admins in the DYK process as defined in the instructions, and the role as practiced, differ widely. Moreover, different admins treat their role differently, and based on past discussions, have widely divergent views on what the role should be. For folks unfamiliar with the process, admins are required to move approved DYK hooks from Prep areas to Queues. The question here is what, if any, further checks admins are required to perform during this process.  

Since there are many possible combinations here, I have structured this to permit maximum flexibility in the outcome. Therefore, please feel free to add additional checks that you think admins are required to do, that I may have left out. [[User:Vanamonde93|Vanamonde]] ([[User talk:Vanamonde93|talk]]) 17:27, 11 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)#rfc_FD8E321|Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)]] expired 2018-03-08 03:01 ===
* Id: FD8E321
* User: Headbomb
* Date: 2018-02-21 12:43:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|826870038|PROJ 826870038}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|826870040|TECH 826870040}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|826870042|PROP 826870042}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|829354433|PROJ 829354433}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|829354435|TECH 829354435}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|829354436|PROP 829354436}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
'''tl;dr version:''' I propose that we change [[:Category:Infobox templates]] to a {{tl|all included}}/{{tl|tracking category}}, and get all the benefits this would entail.

'''Current situation/Proposed solution'''

Currently [[:Category:Infobox templates]] is setup as a {{tl|container category}} [with a handful of infoboxes which are mistakenly in the category], which is pretty much completely useless. Infoboxes are sub-categorized in an extremely incomplete way, so finding anything is almost impossible simply because this scheme is pretty much ignored, on top of just badly designed in general. Try to find something like {{tl|Infobox journal}} from the main category, and you'll be spending a long time browsing things before realizing it's located in
*[[:Category:Infobox templates]]
**[[:Category:Arts and culture infobox templates]]
***[[:Category:Publishing infobox templates]]
or
*[[:Category:Infobox templates]]
**[[:Category:Society and social science infobox templates]]
***[[:Category:Organization infobox templates]]
And that's when it's categorized in the first place. You can't get to {{tl|Infobox ABL team}}, because it's not categorized.

So to fix/improve this situation, I propose that we change [[:Category:Infobox templates]] to a {{tl|all included}}/{{tl|tracking category}}. This would have several benefits, such as (non-exhaustive list):
*All infoboxes would conveniently be listed directly there. If you're looking for something ABL related, you just browse the category and look for ABL. If you're looking for {{tl|Infobox magazine}}, you go in the ''M'' section and look for magazine.
*The category could then be easily searched with an <code>:incategory</code> call in [[:Special:Search]]. If you're looking for a retail-related infobox, you could just search for [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?search=retail+incategory%3A%22Infobox+templates%22&title=Special:Search&profile=all&fulltext=1&searchToken=1n08vfke7nwvxs49sedlq9unx 'retail'], and you'd find {{tl|Infobox retail market}} quite easily.
*The category could then be used to easily monitor recent changes/vandalism via [[:Special:RecentChangesLinked/Category:Infobox templates]].
*The category could then be used by [[WP:AALERTS]] to create article alerts for [[WP:WikiProject Infoboxes]].

The category could be automatically populated and correctly sorted by the {{tl|Infobox}} template itself (and other similar templates) in the vast majority of cases (at the very least anything that starts with ''Template:Infobox foobar'' can be), with the rest being manually categorized. This wouldn't change the subcategory system, so editors could still find {{tl|Infobox element}} via
*[[:Category:Infobox templates]]
**[[:Category:Science and nature infobox templates]]
***[[:Category:Chemistry infobox templates]]
****[[:Category:Periodic table infobox templates]]
if they prefer browsing that way. <span style="font-variant:small-caps; whitespace:nowrap;">[[User:Headbomb|Headbomb]] {[[User talk:Headbomb|t]] · [[Special:Contributions/Headbomb|c]] · [[WP:PHYS|p]] · [[WP:WBOOKS|b]]}</span> 12:43, 21 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Musicians#rfc_C49AAEE|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Musicians]] expired 2018-03-08 05:01 ===
* Id: C49AAEE
* User: 4TheWynne
* Date: 2018-02-06 04:47:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|824245569|MEDIA 824245569}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|829366037|MEDIA 829366037}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I brought up in a [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Musicians/Archive 10#RfC: Band member timelines|previous discussion]] that I would probably do this down the track – and pretty much made most of my argument there – so I figured there's no better time than the present. I've seen bands that have had large numbers of line-up changes (e.g. [[Anthrax (American band)|Anthrax]], [[Black Sabbath]], [[Megadeth]]) and have their own members subpages – this is where I believe it is most appropriate to have them. Others have only had minimal changes or disruptions to their respective line-ups (e.g. [[Foo Fighters]], [[Linkin Park]], [[Pearl Jam]]), yet still have these subpages where they, in my opinion, aren't necessary.

I will restate my opinion (from the above discussion) that '''members subpages should only exist if there have been a large number of line-up changes and/or complex circumstances''' – does anyone agree with this statement? Please answer "'''Yes'''" or "'''No'''" in the survey below and, if agreed upon, use the discussion to discuss what number of line-up changes should constitute a members subpage – otherwise, feel free to state your opinion in either section. I would define "large number of line-up changes and/or complex circumstances" as about ten or more former members and/or line-up changes (criteria met by the first three bands that I mentioned, and not by the second three). <b style="font-family:Arial">[[User:4TheWynne|<span style="color:darkblue">4TheWynne</span>]]<sup>[[User talk:4TheWynne|<span style="color:darkblue">(talk)</span>]][[Special:Contribs/4TheWynne|<span style="color:darkblue">(contribs)</span>]]</sup></b> 04:47, 6 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_7961B80|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2018-03-08 23:02 ===
* Id: 7961B80
* User: Rusf10
* Date: 2018-02-19 01:37:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|826431380|POLICY 826431380}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|829993495|POLICY 829993495}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
===Background'''

Given recent disruption caused by non-admin closures of [[WP:AFD]], I am proposing that non-admin closures/relistings be banned except in very limited circumstances. The most obvious exception being when someone withdraws their own nomination (there may be one or two other exceptions but that's the only one that comes to mind for me). Here are two recent ANIs where someone has created disruption by closing an AfD [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Administrators%27_noticeboard/Incidents#Many_non-admin_AfD_closures_by_User:Jdcomix] & [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Administrators%27_noticeboard/IncidentArchive971#Inappropriate_AfD_closure_by_number_of_votes]. This seems to be a recurring issue and I think this is the best way to deal with it. I understand that admins are busy and others try to help, but it is actually creating more work when someone has to go back and review poor closings/relistings.--[[User:Rusf10|Rusf10]] ([[User talk:Rusf10|talk]]) 01:37, 19 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_8224D26|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2018-03-09 04:01 ===
* Id: 8224D26
* User: TonyBallioni
* Date: 2018-02-20 19:31:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|826746310|POLICY 826746310}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|829522700|POLICY 829522700}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
After being pointed out by Newyorkbrad at AN earlier that we might want to find a streamlined way to deal with community bans for repeated sockmasters to avoid what has become a recent trend of seeking formal bans for them at AN, I began workshopping some language with other users, and would like to propose the following additions be made to [[Wikipedia:Banning policy]]:
{{talkquote|Editors who have been found to have engaged in sockpuppetry on at least two occasions after an initial indefinite block, for whatever reason, are considered ''de facto'' banned by the Wikipedia community. Publicly documented CheckUser evidence should typically be involved before a user is considered banned in this way. Users fitting this criteria are subject to the same unban conditions as users banned by community discussion.{{pb}}Administrators should typically place a notice at Wikipedia:Administrators' Noticeboard alerting the community of such a ban as well as place [[Template:Banned user]] to the master's user page and add the user to any relevant Arbitration Committee sanctions enforcement list.}}
The terms of the proposal would make it so that after three indefinite blocks, a user is considered ''de facto'' banned under the banning policy. [[User:TonyBallioni|TonyBallioni]] ([[User talk:TonyBallioni|talk]]) 19:31, 20 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Ronald Reagan#rfc_135FE16|Talk:Ronald Reagan]] expired 2018-03-09 21:01 ===
* Id: 135FE16
* User: FriendlyRiverOtter
* Date: 2018-03-07 16:57:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|829272444|BIO 829272444}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|829636025|BIO 829636025}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Our article current states: "What neither Deaver nor other administration officials initially realized was that many Germans drew a distinction between the regular SS, who typically were composed of Nazi true believers, and the Waffen-SS which were attached to military units and composed of conscripted soldiers."

But we are not including sources such as the following which state, not so quick, it wasn't so simple.

::[http://www.nytimes.com/1985/04/28/world/ss-unit-s-history-overlooked-in-us-plan-on-german-visit.html?pagewanted=all SS UNIT'S HISTORY OVERLOOKED IN U.S. PLAN ON GERMAN VISIT], ''New York Times'', John Tagliabue, James Markham, April 28, 1985.

So, how do we briefly and accurately summarize why a number of Americans protested President Reagan's visit to the military cemetery in Bitburg, Germany in May 1985? [[User:FriendlyRiverOtter|FriendlyRiverOtter]] ([[User talk:FriendlyRiverOtter|talk]]) 16:57, 7 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Canada#rfc_184A342|Talk:Canada]] expired 2018-03-10 04:01 ===
* Id: 184A342
* User: Cryptic Canadian
* Date: 2018-02-08 03:56:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|824570208|SOC 824570208}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|829685303|SOC 829685303}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The current sound file of the national anthem in the article's infobox is [https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/index.php?title=File%3AFr-%C3%94_Canada.ogg File:Fr-Ô Canada.ogg], a recording that is over a century old. It has a bitrate of ''100 kilobits'', which, combined with its vocals, makes the melody rather difficult to hear. The entire thing is very out of place, given that a) the vocals are also from the French version of the song rather than the English version, which would be easier to understand for most visitors to the ''English'' Wikipedia, and b) on the infoboxes on articles for other countries, instrumental versions of their anthems seem to be far more common.

There are some alternatives available, but usually whenever someone adds them, they get reverted on the basis that consensus has already been established. Going back through the archives of this talk page, there have indeed been discussions on the issue going back to at least 2012, but it seems to be a very weak consensus. One of the main contenders for the replacement is the higher quality [https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:United_States_Navy_Band_-_O_Canada.ogg File:United States Navy Band - O Canada.ogg], but this has proven somewhat controversial: see exhibits [[Talk:Canada/Archive_22#Add_Audio_For_Oh_Canada|A]], [[Talk:Canada/Archive_23#Anthem_sound_file|B]], [[Talk:Canada/Archive_23#O_Canada|C]] [[Talk:Canada/Archive_26#O_Canada_audio|D]], among others I'm likely missing.

The other alternative is  [https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/index.php?title=File%3AO_Canada.ogg File:O Canada.ogg], a simplistic but recognizable piano version, which existed on the article for some time before it was [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canada&diff=prev&oldid=812226946 removed a few months ago] without any explanation, but no longer seems to be [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Canada&diff=823229630&oldid=823225247 the de facto replacement] for the US Navy version.

This seems to be a persistent issue that seems to challenge the consensus that has apparently been established so I've decided to open this up to RFC. <span style="background:#000000;">[[User:Cryptic Canadian|'''<span style="color:red;">Cryptic </span>''']] [[User talk:Cryptic Canadian|'''<span style="color:white;">Canadian</span>''']]</span> 03:56, 8 February 2018 (UTC)}}

<blockquote>
In 2017 after [[Amira Hass]] in her [[Haaretz]] column posted a B'Tselem video and castigated the IDF officer who appeared in the video arresting a man who refused to comply with warnings to leave the area while filming the officer,<ref name="Haaretz20170511"/> [[IDF Spokesperson]] Major General [[Moti Almoz]] said B'Tselem videos are "are out of line with reality" and that "there is a substantial difference between filming an incident as it is happening and the creating of an incident by arriving at a place with a camera".<ref>[https://www.ynetnews.com/articles/0,7340,L-4960278,00.html IDF defends soldier over B'Tselem video], YNET, 10 May 2017</ref><ref name="Haaretz20170511">[https://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/idf-b-tselem-created-incident-for-video-posted-on-haaretz-1.5470753 Israeli Army Says B'Tselem Created Incident for Video Posted on Haaretz], Ha'aretz, Gili Coehn, 11 May 2017</ref><ref>[http://www.jpost.com/Arab-Israeli-Conflict/IDF-spokesman-personally-replies-to-BTselem-slander-490341 IDF Spokesman Posts Personal Resopose to B'Tselem Video], JPost, 10 May 2017</ref><ref>[https://news.walla.co.il/item/3063677 IDF spokesman on B'Tselem video: "provocation disconnected from reality"], Walla news, 10 May 2017</ref><ref>[http://www.mako.co.il/news-military/security-q2_2017/Article-edaa2aa4bd2fb51004.htm IDF vs. B'Tselem: "Libel directed against IDF"], 10 May 2017, Channel 2 News</ref><ref>[http://10tv.nana10.co.il/Article/?ArticleID=1245536 IDF vs. B'Tselem: "Decided a Video is More Important than the Truth], CHannel 10 News, 10 May 2017</ref>
</blockquote>
{{ref-talk}}
Should the follow appear under the "incidents" sub-section?
<blockquote>
In 2010 media outlets published that B'Tselem's information director, prior to her employment in B'Tselem,  wrote on her personal blog various statements such as "The IDF Memorial Day is a pornographic circus", "Israel is committing Humanity's worst atrocities... Israel is proving devotion to Nazi values".<ref>[https://books.google.co.il/books?id=BUXCAqJUdmUC&pg=PA110&lpg=PA110&dq=%22Lizi+Sagie%22&source=bl&ots=aUdmTO8FCt&sig=c2NgI6kc6SZpbZ3NGQTs8dhTF2k&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiHxb6ahNfYAhVFVywKHVTQC_kQ6AEIWjAN#v=onepage&q=%22Lizi%20Sagie%22&f=false Reaping What You Sow: A Comparative Examination of Torture Reform in the United States, France, Argentina, and Israel], Henry F. Carey, 2012, page 110</ref><ref>[https://books.google.co.il/books?id=3ErLCgAAQBAJ&pg=PT187&lpg=PT187&dq=%22lizi+sagie%22&source=bl&ots=1998aga9Qz&sig=IJUbljnusJVzGtlqAwxSib6SFaQ&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjf-puk3ZXZAhUGaxQKHfeMAJkQ6AEIWzAO#v=onepage&q=%22lizi%20sagie%22&f=false Making David into Goliath: How the World Turned Against Israel], Joshua Muravchik,
 2015, page 149</ref><ref name="Globes20100418">[https://www.globes.co.il/news/article.aspx?did=1000553581 Lizi Sagie, senior B'Tselem officer: Israel adheres to Nazi values, and turns its casualties into celebrities, Globes], 18 April 2010</ref> B'Tselem director Jessica Montell said that B'Tselem rejected these statement and that they do not represent B'Tselem,<ref name="Globes20100418"/> and the information director resigned shortly thereafter from her position saying that she apologizes for making hurtful statements and that "veracity and professionalism are B'Tselem's main assets and are essential, I hope that now attention will return to what is truly important: struggling for human rights in the occupied territories".<ref>[http://www.globes.co.il/news/article.aspx?did=1000554369 Lizi Sagie, who called Memorial Day a "pornographic circus", resigns], Globes, 22 April 2010</ref><ref>[http://www.mako.co.il/news-israel/education/Article-bbfecd9e6952821004.htm As a result of her statements: senior B'Tselem figure resigns], Channel 2 News, 22 April 2010</ref>

In August 2014, journalist [[Tuvia Tenenbom]] taped Palestinians and Israeli activists presenting the conflict to foreigners. One of those taped was a B'Tselem field researcher who [[Holocaust denial|denied the Holocaust]] saying "It’s a lie — I don’t believe it".<ref name="Channel2Aug2014">[http://www.mako.co.il/news-channel2/Friday-Newscast/Article-ee534b081f22841004.htm The undercover journalist who revealed the hate to israel], Channel2 News, 29 August 2017</ref> B'Tselem said they rejected holocaust denial and that they would investigate the incident.<ref name="Channel2Aug2014"/> B'Tselem investigation concluded that the field researcher merely translated what an off camera individual had said and said that the field researcher "said unequivocally that the Holocaust is a terrible crime against the Jewish people". However, in October 2014 after a longer segment of the exchange with the field worker was aired,<ref>[http://www.mako.co.il/news-military/politics-q4_2014/Article-4675b07eb24e841004.htm B'Tselem admits: Field researcher denied Holocaust], Channel 2 News, 6 October 2014</ref> B'Tselem said "we ask to amend our [original] response on this matter, which was given in good faith, and clarify that a B’Tselem worker did say those things, which we reject with contempt and disgust".<ref>[https://www.timesofisrael.com/israeli-rights-group-admits-employee-denied-holocaust/ Israeli rights group admits employee denied Holocaust], Times of Israel, 7 October 2014</ref><ref>[http://www.maariv.co.il/news/new.aspx?pn6Vq=11&0r9VQ=GGFHJ The troubling "truth" of B'Tselem], Maariv, 7 October 2014</ref> B'Tselem terminated the employment of the field researcher.<ref>[https://www.btselem.org/about_btselem/accusations_regarding_former_btselem_employee Response to accusations regarding former B'Tselem's field Researcher 'Atef Abu a-Rub], B'Tselem, 7 October 2014</ref>
</blockquote>
{{ref-talk}}

* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
"While USPSTF has reversed their complete opposition to PCa screening they still recommend against it for those who are 70 or older.[11]" This content passes verification without using the additional source that fails to verify "reversed their complete opposition".[https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Prostate_cancer&type=revision&diff=828990648&oldid=828900194]

"Such screening is controversial[90] and, for many, may lead to unnecessary disruption and possibly harmful consequences.[91]" Unsupported weasel word was removed and each citation is placed where they verify each claim.[https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Prostate_cancer&type=revision&diff=828990648&oldid=828900194] [[User:QuackGuru|<b style="color: #e34234;">QuackGuru</b>]] ([[User talk:QuackGuru|<span style="color: #B02200;">talk</span>]]) 00:07, 6 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:List of oldest living people#rfc_1042DE9|Talk:List of oldest living people]] expired 2018-03-13 04:01 ===
* Id: 1042DE9
* User: DerbyCountyinNZ
* Date: 2018-02-11 03:13:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|825070900|BIO 825070900}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|830165358|BIO 830165358}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
See above regarding Maria Emilia Quesada. This person has been removed on the basis that 1 or more editors don't believe the claim is genuine. Whether or not it is genuine is not up to editors to decide. The criteria for inclusion in this article is that the person is a) old enough to make the list b) has been reported alive within the last year yb a [[WP:RS|reliable source]] and c) is not older than the oldest living person as announced by Guinness. The reasons for these criteria are given [[Talk:List of oldest living people/Archive 16#Clarification/discussion of requirements for inclusion, retention and removal from this list|here]]. Editors opinions that anyone should be excluded while meeting this criteria is pure [[WP:POV]] and needs to be actively discouraged. Seeking input from impartial and experienced editors as to whether [[WP:IDONTLIKEIT]] is sufficient to over-ride or change consensus. [[User:DerbyCountyinNZ|<span style="background:orange; color:blue">DerbyCountyinNZ</span>]] <sup>([[User talk:DerbyCountyinNZ|Talk]] [[Special:Contribs/DerbyCountyinNZ|Contribs]])</sup> 03:13, 11 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:The National Memo#rfc_9F92FB6|Talk:The National Memo]] expired 2018-03-13 11:01 ===
* Id: 9F92FB6
* Date: 2018-02-11 10:53:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|825082839|MEDIA 825082839}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|825082841|POL 825082841}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|830199159|MEDIA 830199159}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|830199161|POL 830199161}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Following the advice from {{u|Robert McClenon}} I'm making this request for comment concerning [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:The_National_Memo#Several_edits the proposed edits above]. Before making this request I've discussed these changes at the article's Talk page, created the discussion at [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:WikiProject_Journalism#Help_with_the_National_memo_article Project Journalism] and filed [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Dispute_resolution_noticeboard#Talk:The_National_Memo#Several_edits dispute resolution request].

I would like third-party view on including proposed edits to the article as we are unable to reach the consensus here, at the Talk page.

''' Summary of the discussion '''

After substantial edits from {{u|Justlettersandnumbers}} an important information describing the media's political stance was removed from the article. The editor first removed the phrase ''predominantly from a liberal perspective'' and changed it to ''predominantly from a left-wing point of view''. When asked to provide solid references, supporting this point of view, he agreed to drop his initial ''left-wing'' claim. As a result of edits from {{u|Spintendo}} the article now doesn't have any information describing the political/editorial stance of [[The National Memo]] as a media. It is important to mention that '''before I made any edits to the article''' it has the following consensus edits result: ''[https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_National_Memo&oldid=786863699 it features daily breaking news and commentary as well as analysis from America's top progressive thinkers from a liberal / progressive perspective]''. I would like to re-instate the truth as both ''liberal'' and ''progressive'' statements are well-supported by references to high-quality third-party sources (unlike other claims such as ''left-wing''). I also think that this information is important to Wikipedia users/readers because after the extensive edits (or rather deletions) from {{u|Justlettersandnumbers}} it is hard to understand what [[The National Memo]] is about. There are several editors (notably {{u|Justlettersandnumbers}} and {{u|Spintendo}} who think that this information should me omitted from the article. - 10:53, 11 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Criteria for speedy deletion#rfc_F9B9A1A|Wikipedia talk:Criteria for speedy deletion]] expired 2018-03-13 20:01 ===
* Id: F9B9A1A
* Date: 2018-02-23 16:59:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|827250401|POLICY 827250401}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|830268549|POLICY 830268549}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
It has always seemed strange to me that we can freely delete articles created by someone banned by the community, but not explicitly for someone banned by the Terms of Use, though G5 could certainly be interpreted in that way. I see two options:

; G5. Creations by banned or blocked users
{{Further|Wikipedia:Banning policy|Wikipedia:Blocking policy|Wikipedia:Terms of use}}
This applies to pages created by [[:Category:Banned Wikipedia users|banned]] or [[:Category:Blocked Wikipedia users|blocked]] users''' either in violation of their [[Wikipedia:Banning policy|ban]] or [[Wikipedia:Blocking policy|block]] or by virtue of violation of the Wikimedia Foundation Terms of Use''', and that have no substantial edits by others. G5 should not be applied to [[WP:TRANS|transcluded]] templates or to [[WP:CATEGORY|categories]] that may be useful or suitable for merging. For a banned or blocked user:
* To qualify, an edit or article must have been made while the user was actually banned or blocked. A page created before the ban or block was imposed or after it was lifted will not qualify under this criterion.
* To qualify, the edit must be a violation of the user's specific block or ban. Pages created by a topic-banned user may be deleted if they come under that particular topic, but not if they are legitimately about some other topic.
* {{Tlp|Db-g5|''name of banned user''}}, {{Tlp|Db-banned|''name of banned user''}}

; Gx. Violation of Terms of use
{{Further|Wikipedia:Terms of use}}
This applies to pages created in violation of the [[:Wikimedia:Terms of Use|Wikimedia Foundation terms of use]], and that have no substantial edits by others. 

To qualify, the edit or article must have been made by a user demonstrated or admitted to be in violation of the Terms of Use. Specific categories of violation include:
* Harassing and Abusing Others
* Violating the Privacy of Others
* Engaging in False Statements, Impersonation, or Fraud
* Committing Infringement
* Misusing Our Services for Other Illegal Purposes
* Engaging in Disruptive and Illegal Misuse of Facilities
* Paid contributions without disclosure
The article must have been created by an editor in violation of the terms of use and have no substantive content edits by others. 
<b>[[User Talk:JzG|Guy]]</b> <small>([[User:JzG/help|Help!]])</small> 16:59, 23 February 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|830507290|BIO 830507290}}

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|830507294|POLICY 830507294}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|830512055|BIO 830512055}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Religion_and_philosophy|prev|830512086|RELI 830512086}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|830512089|POLICY 830512089}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
{{collapse bottom}}
Preamble: The majoritarian idea of governance often has the provision that certain majoritarian actions might be infringing on minority groups, which is to say the actions are persecutory, and therefore statutes have to be put in place to either limit majoritarian rampages, or else protect minority interests specifically. 

The RFC to remove the religion= tag from the main infobox might have come about without fair treatment of the minority opinion, and so I propose two things, that the religion= tag be restored and a guideline for its usage be written. In addition, I make the suggestion that Arbcom review the RFC in order to form guidelines to protect minority interests from majoritarian sweeps, such that as in this case, other solutions were not sought or taken. 

On the matter of the RFC and its claimed validity, the validity naturally rests entirely on the idea of it being majoritarian, and a "snow close" issue. But then atheist majoritarianism would have the problem that it would wipe away religion as a topical element from articles project wide, and that has to be prevented, by statue and guideline. 

The internet seems to have a strong showing of atheists and science-culturists, but if science culture is taking the form of an irrational cult religion, and atheism is not really a personal view but an increasingly more organized anti-religion movement, then these things need to be countered with some common sense that rejects POV movements and does honorable treatment of the human condition and the role religion has played in it. -[[User:Inowen|Inowen]] ([[User talk:Inowen|talk]]) 06:15, 15 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Type 4 Chi-To#rfc_23F003A|Talk:Type 4 Chi-To]] expired 2018-03-15 19:01 ===
* Id: 23F003A
* Date: 2018-02-14 18:22:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|825674808|HIST 825674808}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|830586336|HIST 830586336}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I noticed that in the [[:Category:World War II tanks by country]] there's a great differentiation in how the individual articles are named. According to [[WP:NAMINGCRITERIA]]: ''"a title usually conveys what the subject is actually called in English."'' Respectively, in the [[:Category:World War II tanks of the United States]] (which is perhaps the most representative to English language articles on the subject), most articles have the word "tank" included in their titles: [[T14 Heavy Tank]], [[T20 Medium Tank]], [[T28 Super Heavy Tank]], [[T29 Heavy Tank]], [[T30 Heavy Tank]], and so on. By contrast, in the [[:Category:World War II tanks of Japan]] the word "tank" is never (!) used in the title of their models, i.e.: [[Type 1 Chi-He]], [[Type 1 Ho-Ni I]], [[Type 2 Ho-I]], [[Type 2 Ka-Mi]], [[Type 2 Ke-To]], [[Type 3 Chi-Nu]], and so on. I would suggest that some kind of linguistic uniformity here be followed throughout, for the benefit of our readership. Wouldn't you agree? —  '''[[User:Poeticbent|<span style="color:darkblue;font-family:Papyrus">Poeticbent</span>]]''' [[User_talk:Poeticbent|<span style="color:#FFFFFF;font-size:7.0pt;font-weight:bold;background:#FF88AF;border:1px solid #DF2929;padding:0.0em 0.2em;">talk</span>]] 18:22, 14 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Kingdom of France#rfc_A16B9CF|Talk:Kingdom of France]] expired 2018-03-19 09:01 ===
* Id: A16B9CF
* User: Conservatrix
* Date: 2018-03-03 21:30:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|828647524|HIST 828647524}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|828647529|POL 828647529}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|831196075|HIST 831196075}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|831196078|POL 831196078}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
'''Background''': The Kingdom of France as made in the image of [[Hugh Capet]] held at its foundation the practice of [[Salic Law]], manifest in the [[French dynastic disputes|''Arrêt Lemaistre'' and Fundamental Laws of France]], which constituted the monarchical succession for over eight-hundred years. These traditions were immutable and considered vital to the existence of the State. However, the [[French Revolution]] of 1789 abolished this traditional succession, favoring a constitutional alternative that was to re-emerge in the [[July Revolution]] of 1830. This nineteenth-century uprising saw the Bourbon monarchy deposed in favor of [[Louis Philippe I|Louis Philippe d'Orléans]] as "King of the French", his realm designated the "French Kingdom", to better associate the government with its people and the [[Declaration of the Rights of Man and of the Citizen|revolutionary reforms]] of 1789.

'''Proposal''': We should divide the Kingdom of France and French Kingdom into two separate articles, drawing clear distinction between the Salic-foundational and [[Charter of 1830|Charte-foundational]] monarchies. This can be realized by relocating all relevant information to the [[July Monarchy]] page.

<sub>NOTE: The [[Kingdom of France (1791–92)| Kingdom of France 1791–92]] would best be described as a government in captivity given that [[Louis XVI]] was incapacitated as a prisoner of circumstance; juxtaposed to the rule of Louis Philippe in 1830, who was free to govern and travel of his own volition, it would not be appropriate to separate the 1791-92 article.</sub><p>- [[User:Conservatrix|Conservatrix]] ([[User talk:Conservatrix|talk]]) 21:30, 3 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Greek royal family#rfc_E7DAD30|Talk:Greek royal family]] expired 2018-03-19 11:01 ===
* Id: E7DAD30
* User: The Gnome
* Date: 2018-02-17 10:58:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|826132027|BIO 826132027}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|826132028|HIST 826132028}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|826132030|POL 826132030}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|826132033|SOC 826132033}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|831207868|BIO 831207868}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|831207871|HIST 831207871}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|831207876|POL 831207876}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|831207877|SOC 831207877}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The title of the article does not seem to conform to [[WP:COMMMONNAME|the rule about articles' names]]. To remind ourselves of the pertinent passage in the rule, here it is: "''Wikipedia generally prefers the name that is most commonly used (as determined by its prevalence in a significant majority of independent, reliable English-language sources) as such names will usually best fit the [[WP:NAMINGCRITERIA|[naming] criteria]]. ... Wikipedia does not necessarily use the subject's "official" name as an article title; it generally prefers to use the name that is most frequently used to refer to the subject in English-language reliable sources.''"

The name most commonly used by the overwhelming majority of [[WP:RS|reliable sources]] is "the former royal family of Greece" (or equivalent expressions, such as "former royal household"). Typical such citations can be found in the [[BBC]] (e.g. [http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/6289097.stm here]); ''[[Washington Post]]'' ([http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2007/01/24/AR2007012401325.html here]); the ''[[National Herald]]'' ([https://www.thenationalherald.com/wp-content/uploads/2013/11/673.pdf here]); [[Canadian Broadcasting Corporation|CBC]] News ([http://www.cbc.ca/news/entertainment/christie-s-begins-antiquities-sale-over-objections-of-greece-1.654941 here]); the ''[[Daily Telegraph]]'', UK  ([http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/uknews/1535659/Exiled-Greek-royals-sell-off-the-family-silver.html here]); the ''[[The Daily Telegraph (Sydney)|Daily Telegraph]]'', Australia ([https://www.escape.com.au/where-the-wealthy-unwind-spetses-paradise-for-the-rich-in-the-greek-islands/news-story/e16d1699e03ac455ae450d411910b6e5 here]); ''[[The Guardian]]'' ([https://www.theguardian.com/artanddesign/2007/jan/24/art.world here]); all the English-language online editions of newspapers, magazines, and other media in Greece (e.g. [http://greece.greekreporter.com/2010/08/25/european-royals-gather-for-greek-island-wedding%E2%80%8E/ here], [http://en.protothema.gr/former-greek-royal-family-dined-at-the-acropolis-museum/ here], or [http://www.ekathimerini.com/35921/article/ekathimerini/news/culture-ministry-explores-contents-of-old-royal-estate here]). Plus, all English Wikipedia articles concerning members of the family (e.g. about [[Constantine II of Greece]] or [[Tatoi Palace]]) use the term "former".

The historical, official appellation is used mostly by fringe [[royalist]] organizations, media, and political parties (e.g. [http://www.greekroyalfamily.gr/en.html The Greek Royal Family]; [http://www.theroyalforums.com/forums/f24/princes-and-princesses-of-greece-and-denmark-8863.html Royal Forums]; [https://royalcorrespondent.com/category/greek-royal-family/ Royal Correspondent]; etc) or [[gossip magazine]]s, such as ''[[Hello (magazine)|Hello]]'' (see [https://www.hellomagazine.com/tags/greek-royal-wedding/ here]) or ''Life & Style'' (e.g. [http://www.lifeandstylemag.com/tags/royal-family-20153 here]).

It is suggested that the title of this article changes accordingly.</br>

=== [[Talk:Muslim conquests of the Indian subcontinent#rfc_9398DF2|Talk:Muslim conquests of the Indian subcontinent]] expired 2018-03-19 21:01 ===
* Id: 9398DF2
* User: 202.156.182.84
* Date: 2018-03-17 13:55:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|831274959|UNSORTED 831274959}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|831292702|UNSORTED 831292702}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
A large amount of the text already included shows that the numerous invasions were either defeated, repelled or they were just short opportunistic raids. Wikipedia guidelines on neutrality, POV, bias, due balance, etc are clear. Calling those the "conquests" is POV bias, which lends undue balance to some "wins" against the "numerous" defeats / repulsions /expulsions of muslim invaders by the native hindus/sikhs/buddhists. The contentious namespace, such as the [[Muslim conquests of the Indian subcontinent]], creates a muslim-supremacist bias. Move the article to a more non-contentious, balanced, fairer, and more accurate non-supremacist namespace, such as the [[Attempted muslim invasions of the Indian subcontinent]] or the [[Muslim invasions of the Indian subcontinent]], etc. [[Special:Contributions/202.156.182.84|202.156.182.84]] ([[User talk:202.156.182.84|talk]]) 13:55, 17 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Sex#rfc_FA78838|Talk:Sex]] expired 2018-03-20 09:01 ===
* Id: FA78838
* User: Flyer22 Reborn
* Date: 2018-02-18 08:42:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|826291781|SCI 826291781}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|826291783|SOC 826291783}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|831383510|SCI 831383510}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|831383512|SOC 831383512}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
In [[Talk:Sex#WP:Undue intersex material in the lead|a discussion]] higher up on the article talk page, concern has been expressed about the lead sentence of the article. '''One view''' is that "splitting things into male/female/intersex is far too human centric - far more generally relevant is male/female/hermaphrodite." In a similar vein, there is also sentiment that stating "are specialized into male and female varieties, each known as a sex" makes the article "overly narrowed [...] to be about biological sex, which is far narrower than the subject of the article. This was always intended to be the general article, where the various meanings of sex are explained, distinguished, and linked to." The '''other view''' is that when sources on "sex" are not talking about sexual intercourse/other sexual activity or sociological gender, they are talking about biological/anatomical sex, which are terms that redirect to this article and do not solely concern humans. There are already [[Sexual intercourse]], [[Sexual activity]], [[Sexual reproduction]] and [[Gender]] articles. This article is mainly about biological/anatomical sex. It is not an article for every definition of sex that exists. [[Sex (disambiguation)]] covers that. Per [[WP:Lead sentence]], this article's first sentence should be clear what it's about. 

So which lead sentence should we go with?

'''Option 1''': "[[Organism]]s of many [[species]] are specialized into male and female varieties, each known as a '''sex'''."

'''Option 2''': "[[Sexual reproduction]] involves the combining and mixing of [[genetics|genetic]] traits: specialized [[Cell (biology)|cells]] known as [[gamete]]s combine to form offspring that inherit traits from each parent."

'''Option 3''': Some other wording.

I'll alert [[WP:Biology]], [[WP:Physiology]], [[WP:Anatomy]] and [[WP:Med]] to this discussion. Sources are listed in the [[Talk:Sex#Discussion|Discussion]] section below. [[User:Flyer22 Reborn|Flyer22 Reborn]] ([[User talk:Flyer22 Reborn|talk]]) 08:42, 18 February 2018 (UTC)}}

* Version A:

{{talkquote|In his initial statement on the rally, Trump did not denounce white nationalists but instead condemned "hatred, bigotry, and violence on many sides". His statement and his subsequent defenses of it, in which he also referred to "very fine people on both sides", suggested a moral equivalence between the white supremacist marchers and those who protested against them, leading some observers to state that he was sympathetic to white supremacy.<ref name="nyt-boost">{{cite news |work=The New York Times |title=Trump Gives White Supremacists an Unequivocal Boost |first1=Glenn |last1=Thrush |first2=Maggie |last2=Haberman |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/08/15/us/politics/trump-charlottesville-white-nationalists.html |date=August 15, 2017 |deadurl=no |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20170817120257/https://www.nytimes.com/2017/08/15/us/politics/trump-charlottesville-white-nationalists.html |archivedate=August 17, 2017 |df=mdy-all}}</ref>
}}
and
{{talkquote|Ten days after the rally, in prepared remarks at an [[American Legion]] conference, Trump called for the country to unite. He said: "We are not defined by the color of our skin, the figure on our paycheck or the party of our politics. Rather, we are defined by our shared humanity, our citizenship in this magnificent nation and by the love that fills our hearts."<ref>{{cite news|last1=Fabian|first1=Jordan|title=After divisive rally, Trump calls for unity|url=http://thehill.com/homenews/administration/347689-after-divisive-rally-trump-calls-for-unity|newspaper=The Hill |date=August 23, 2017 |accessdate=January 16, 2018}}</ref>

=== [[Template talk:Marriage#rfc_953AFF3|Template talk:Marriage]] expired 2018-03-22 16:01 ===
* Id: 953AFF3
* Date: 2018-02-20 15:19:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|826705158|STYLE 826705158}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|831870067|STYLE 831870067}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The previous RfC on this topic has caused more confusion than it has solved any issues. By not clarifying that the marriage ended upon the death of the subject of the article (although acknowledged in the article itself) causes issues as it implies the marriage has persisted after death. Additionally, if the spouse of the subject were to remarry, if people click around and skip over details it could suggest that the person in question is in two relationships at once which causes a whole stream of issues in itself. The original his death, her death thing was clearer than the layout being suggested by the discussion above. For articles where this is the case see [[Henry_VIII_of_England|Henry VIII]] where it clarifies and does not cause the confusion, a similar example is in [[Robert_Mugabe|Robert Mugabe's]] article. <br>So to summarise, the formatting used in the case of Henry VIII and Robert Mugabe is better than the discussed format above. Thoughts? [[User:ChieftanTartarus|Chieftain Tartarus]] [[User Talk:ChieftanTartarus|(talk)]] 15:19, 20 February 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
Recently I made two identical edits in which I [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Taiwan&diff=832042730&oldid=832030256 restored] the content that was previously removed by {{u|Szqecs}} and {{u|Phlar}}, both of whom claimed it was "controversial".(see revision history) Nevertheless, in my revision, what was added was only the fact that Taiwan is a partially recognized state and one major establishing event that this state was expelled from the UN in 1971. I cannot understand why this is even "controversial" given that other articles of [[List of states with limited recognition|states with limited recognition]] like [[Republic of Artsakh]], [[Kosovo]], and [[Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic]] all follow the same pattern. Please post your comment on whether those content should be removed. --[[User:Aisakano|Aisakano]] ([[User talk:Aisakano|talk]]) 03:56, 24 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)#rfc_E672FDA|Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)]] expired 2018-03-26 10:01 ===
* Id: E672FDA
* User: KATMAKROFAN
* Date: 2018-03-18 20:20:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|831115466|PROP 831115466}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|832490090|PROP 832490090}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The "open proxy" policy is way too broad. Why are hardblocks (using templates like {{tl|colocationwebhost}} and its cousins) almost always used for VPNs, instead of the softblocks given to other shared IPs? My proposal would change this:
#The open proxy policy would be changed, so that softblocks are applied to offending IPs.
#An adminbot would be created to change all openproxy, colocationwebhost, etc. hardblocks to softblocks (using the {{tl|anonblock}} template).
#After the adminbot was finished, the openproxy, colocationwebhost, etc. templates would be gradually deprecated over the course of 3 to 6 months, and then redirected to the anonblock template.
[[User:KATMAKROFAN|KMF]] ([[User talk:KATMAKROFAN|talk]]) 20:20, 18 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Moscow Paveletskaya railway station#rfc_2213B66|Talk:Moscow Paveletskaya railway station]] expired 2018-03-26 12:01 ===
* Id: 2213B66
* User: TastyPoutine
* Date: 2018-02-24 11:25:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Language_and_linguistics|prev|827383556|LANG 827383556}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|827383592|STYLE 827383592}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Language_and_linguistics|prev|832502927|LANG 832502927}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|832502929|STYLE 832502929}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Looking for thoughts on the names of the Moscow railway stations. A couple of years ago all of the stations were renamed with little apparent discussion. The name of the station in Russian is Paveletsky Vokzal ([[ru:Павелецкий вокзал]]. Although the word “station” in Russian is feminine and would take Paveletskaya skaya as a modifier, such as when you refer to a Metro station like [[Paveletskaya (Zamoskvoretskaya line)]] or [[ru:Павелецкая (станция метро, Замоскворецкая линия)]] , when you refer to a major railway terminal such as this, the modifier should refer to the masculine word “Vokzal” and would take Paveletsky. I’m not entirely sure what the logic behind the move to the feminine version was. But I propose to make these linguistically correct. The stations are:
*[[Moscow Kazanskaya railway station]]
*[[Moscow Kiyevskaya railway station]]
*[[Moscow Kurskaya railway station]]
*[[Moscow Paveletskaya railway station]]
*[[Moscow Rizhskaya railway station]]
*[[Moscow Savyolovskaya railway station]]
*[[Moscow Yaroslavskaya railway station]]

Further, on two articles, [[Moscow Passazhirskaya railway station]] and [[Moscow Smolenskaya railway station]] the names don’t even comport to the name of the facility. As far as I can tell, the names used refer to the stop on the rail line. To me this would be like reading a timetable for a train that terminates at New York-Penn Station and naming the article that rather than [[Pennsylvania Station]] as the facility is officially called. I would propose to rename all of the articles after the proper names [[Belorussky railway station]] and [[Leningradsky railway station]].

'''[[User:TastyPoutine|<span style="color: blue;">TastyPoutine</span>]]''' <sup>[[User talk:TastyPoutine|<span style="color: red;">talk (if you dare)</span>]]</sup> 11:25, 24 February 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Bitcoin#rfc_A4E45C5|Talk:Bitcoin]] expired 2018-03-31 10:01 ===
* Id: A4E45C5
* User: Ladislav Mecir
* Date: 2018-03-01 09:10:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Economy,_trade,_and_companies|prev|828233282|ECON 828233282}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|828233285|SCI 828233285}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Economy,_trade,_and_companies|prev|833404959|ECON 833404959}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|833404963|SCI 833404963}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Edit [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bitcoin&diff=827910419&oldid=827910174] introduced a reliably sourced claim (see ''The New York Times'' article citation<ref name=nyt-split /> below) that up until July 2017, bitcoin users maintained a common set of rules for the cryptocurrency (i.e. that the Bitcoin Cash split was actually the first one). The wording of the last paragraph of the section was <blockquote>Up until July 2017, bitcoin users maintained a common set of rules for the cryptocurrency.<ref name=nyt-split>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/07/25/business/dealbook/bitcoin-cash-split.html|title=Some Bitcoin Backers Are Defecting to Create a Rival Currency|last=Popper|first=Nathaniel|date=25 July 2017|work=The New York Times|access-date=1 March 2018|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> On 1 August 2017, a change of rules was introduced. Since the new rules are not recognized as valid by the old software, the change is referred to as a ''[[Fork (blockchain)#Hard fork|hard fork]]''. The cryptocurrency following the updated rules is called [[Bitcoin Cash]]. Bitcoin Cash has a larger block size limit and had an identical blockchain at the time of fork.<ref>{{cite web |last1 = Radcliffe |first1 = Brent |title = Bitcoin Cash |url = https://www.investopedia.com/terms/b/bitcoin-cash.asp |website = Investopedia |accessdate = 8 December 2017 |date = 20 September 2017 |deadurl = no |archiveurl = https://web.archive.org/web/20171209100013/https://www.investopedia.com/terms/b/bitcoin-cash.asp |archivedate = 9 December 2017 |df = dmy-all }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last1=Tepper|first1=Fitz|title=WTF is bitcoin cash and is it worth anything?|url=https://techcrunch.com/2017/08/02/wtf-is-bitcoin-cash-and-is-it-worth-anything/|website=TechCrunch|accessdate=5 December 2017|language=en|deadurl=no|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20171210223807/https://techcrunch.com/2017/08/02/wtf-is-bitcoin-cash-and-is-it-worth-anything/|archivedate=10 December 2017|df=dmy-all}}</ref> On 12 November another hard fork, [[Bitcoin Gold]], was created. Bitcoin Gold changes the proof-of-work algorithm used in mining.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Reiff|first1=Nathan|title=Bitcoin Gold Is Now Live|url=https://www.investopedia.com/news/bitcoin-gold-now-live/|website=Investopedia|accessdate=29 December 2017|date=13 November 2017|deadurl=no|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20171229231608/https://www.investopedia.com/news/bitcoin-gold-now-live/|archivedate=29 December 2017|df=dmy-all}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Bitcoin Gold, the latest Bitcoin fork, explained|url=https://arstechnica.com/tech-policy/2017/11/bitcoin-gold-the-latest-bitcoin-fork-explained/|website=Ars Technica|accessdate=29 December 2017|language=en-us|deadurl=no|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20171229172206/https://arstechnica.com/tech-policy/2017/11/bitcoin-gold-the-latest-bitcoin-fork-explained/|archivedate=29 December 2017|df=dmy-all}}</ref></blockquote>
{{reflist-talk}}

=== [[Talk:Star Wars: The Last Jedi#rfc_01B0BAA|Talk:Star Wars: The Last Jedi]] expired 2018-03-31 20:01 ===
* Id: 01B0BAA
* User: Toa Nidhiki05
* Date: 2018-03-01 19:25:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|828306029|MEDIA 828306029}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|833477073|MEDIA 833477073}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
We've now [[Talk:Star Wars: The Last Jedi#RfC: Which version of the Audience response section should we go with?|reached consensus on the base version to use for the audience response section]]. It's now time to discuss potential changes. Modifications were suggested to the base text in the RfC; most of these revolved around versions of the text included in version 2. The two options in the RfC were:

'''Version 1/3:'''
<blockquote>Particularly divisive was the reveal that Rey's parents are insignificant;[7][13][15] '''many fans had expected her to be Luke's daughter or to share a lineage with another character from the original trilogy.'''[16][17] There was also sentiment that Snoke's character was underdeveloped '''and that Luke's actions contrasted his previous heroic portrayal'''.[15][18][19] Reviewers stated that fan theories were held so strongly among some viewers that it was difficult for them to accept different stories.[13][15][19] However, other viewers appreciated the film's action, tone and deviation from Star Wars tradition.[13][15]</blockquote>

'''Version 2:'''
<blockquote>Particularly divisive was the reveal that Rey's parents are insignificant;[7][13][15] '''many fans had expected her to share a lineage with another character from the original trilogy'''.[17] There was also sentiment that Snoke's character was underdeveloped '''and disagreement with Luke's portrayal and character arc in whether he was heroic enough'''.[15][18][15][19] Reviewers stated that fan theories were held so strongly among some viewers that it was difficult for them to accept different stories.[13][15][19] However, other viewers appreciated the film's action, tone and deviation from Star Wars tradition.[13][15]</blockquote>

Specifically, the question was whether or not the "Rey is Luke's daughter" fan theory should be mentioned and how to characterize Luke's portrayal. This issue was not decided upon in the RfC; the closer specifically said that .

The question in this RfC, then, is to decide this. '''Should the third paragraph in the audience reception section use the text from Versions 1/3, or the text from version 2'''? '''[[User:Toa Nidhiki05|<i style="color: green; font-family: Mistral;">Toa</i>]] [[User talk:Toa Nidhiki05|<i style="color: green; font-family: Mistral;">Nidhiki05</i>]]''' 19:25, 1 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Manual of Style/Military history#rfc_0F9DAC8|Wikipedia talk:Manual of Style/Military history]] expired 2018-04-03 17:01 ===
* Id: 0F9DAC8
* User: Nilfanion
* Date: 2018-03-04 16:10:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|828764687|STYLE 828764687}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|834042701|STYLE 834042701}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Per [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Military history#Use of decisive|discussion]] at [[WP:MILHIST]], around issues caused by the use of the terms described below which have led to several disputes and edit warring, I propose the following is added to this page (as a subsection of Usage and style):
<blockquote>
'''Results'''

When describing the outcome of a military event, care needs to be taken to avoid [[Wikipedia:original research|original research]]. Terms like "decisive victory", "marginal victory", "tactical victory" can have different meanings in different sources. For instance, a battle described as decisive may have directly led to the conclusion of the conflict, led to a change in direction of the broader conflict, had a clear tactical outcome on the battlefield with no lasting strategic implications, or a number of other possibilities.

These terms should only be used when they reflect a consensus in relevant [[Wikipedia:reliable sources|reliable sources]]. When these terms are used in articles they should have sufficient context from the surrounding text to make their meaning clear. They may also be used as part of a direct quotation from a specific person. They should not be used in an infobox, as there is no ability to give a broader explanation in that location.
</blockquote>

I believe this draft supports editors in dealing with broader issues around these terms (that different sources can and will use them in different ways), and directly addresses the most problematic uses (in infoboxes).--[[User:Nilfanion|Nilf]][[commons:User:Nilfanion|anion]] ([[User talk:Nilfanion|talk]]) 16:10, 4 March 2018 (UTC)}}

Do we '''really''' need all this bureaucracy for stub templates? I don't think so. You want to create a new stub template? You have to go through WSS first. What's that, you've decided to just be bold and create the template? Too bad; it's going to TFD, where the 5 active TFDers will ignore it, causing it to be automaticallly deleted. I propose that WSS be shut down and the stub template process be made much less process-y, per the Esperanza precedent. (This was originally on MFD, but I was told to go here, despite MFD being where the dissolution of Esperanza was discussed.) === [[Talk:People's Mujahedin of Iran#rfc_7688326|Talk:People's Mujahedin of Iran]] expired 2018-04-06 14:01 ===

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|832425047|POL 832425047}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This article comes across as having some obvious [[WP:NPOV]] and [[Weasel word]] issues. I've tried to clean up a couple of sections, but this seems to upset [[user:Pahlevun]], who appears to have monopolized the article. I've tried to take the debate to the article's Talk page, but consensus hasn't been reached with user Pahlevun (though [[user:Icewhiz]] did support proposed changes). I think that at this point we need another neutral editor to have a look at this. What I've found, basically, is that:

1) Biased references are being used to support biased statements (these biased references often seem to be connected to the Iranian regime. As Icewhiz pointed out: Note the Iranian regime (and regime controlled media in Iran) views MEK in a highly negative fashion (MEK being on of the regular "bogeymen" in coverage, regularly assigned blame for various woes). This sometimes seeps into non-Iranian coverage (in proper sources - attributed back to the Iranian regime) - however we should be careful to attribute such negative statements here

2) Other references are being used to support negative statements that are not in the references themselves (see discussion above).

I've tried to discuss this with [[user:Pahlevun]] (see above), but he/she has opted to open an [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Sockpuppet_investigations/Atlantic12 SPI case] against me instead. [[User:London Hall|London Hall]] ([[User talk:London Hall|talk]]) 11:25, 24 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:David Ogden Stiers#rfc_3FE3656|Talk:David Ogden Stiers]] expired 2018-04-08 22:01 ===
* Id: 3FE3656
* User: ResultingConstant
* Date: 2018-03-09 21:48:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|829644087|BIO 829644087}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|829644090|MEDIA 829644090}}

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|829644101|POLICY 829644101}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|835469094|BIO 835469094}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|835469097|MEDIA 835469097}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|835469165|SOC 835469165}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|835469167|POLICY 835469167}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
A brief history of this story : 
* In 1997 "Philedelphia Citypaper" published an interview which said that stiers  was asked if he was gay, and replied  that he was not. {{tq|Are you gay? No, I'm not. But, I believe that we're all the same person differently expressed}} [https://web.archive.org/web/20151014062015/http://citypaper.net/articles/021397/article001.shtml]
* In 2009, the  blog "gossip boy" published an interview which purports to be with Stiers, in which Stiers came out. {{tq|GB: You are gay. Right, David? DOS: Yes, I am. Very proud to be so.}}[https://web.archive.org/web/20090604020126/http://www.gossip-boy.com/DOS.html]
* The gossip boy story was subsequently picked up by '''many''' other sources, which cited the blog . ABC story here :  [http://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/Movies/story?id=7518323&page=1]
* A prior informal RFC was closed without consensus to include [[Talk:David_Ogden_Stiers/Archives/2014]]
* After Stiers death, the story made the rounds again (many sources again), including the NYT obit  (explicitly citing the ABC story above, which cites gossip boy) [https://www.nytimes.com/2018/03/04/obituaries/david-ogden-stiers-mash-dies.html] Or see the TimesUK story which uses direct quotes from the blog, but does not cite any sources and uses their own voice. [https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/david-ogden-stiers-p6kx0dn9k]

{{collapsetop|unreliable info which may or may not shed light on the reliability of the blog}}
* In 2009 wikipedia Accounts ''claiming'' to be PR reps of stiers made comments indicating the interview was fake [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=David_Ogden_Stiers&diff=prev&oldid=287891697][https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=David_Ogden_Stiers&diff=prev&oldid=288088181] (Account was subsequently banned due to not complying with username policy as "group" name)
* During prior discussions of this content, wiki editor {{u|Red Act}} claim to have called Stier's PR firm where they told him the story was false [[Talk:David_Ogden_Stiers/Archives/2013#Gay?]]
* On internet forums, those who claim to be in the know argue that Stiers is in fact gay, but that the interview was false [https://www.datalounge.com/thread/8924141-david-ogden-stiers-n]
{{collapsebottom}}


# '''Does the gossip boy interview (bolstered by otherwise reliable sources which have copied the story) comply with policy ([[WP:BLP]]  (in particular [[WP:GRAPEVINE]]) [[WP:RS]]) sufficient to ''allow'' inclusion of this story in this [[WP:BDP]]'''
# '''If the information meets policy, How should this information be presented''' :
## A. Not included
## B. Describe conflicting interviews, and possible sourcing issues
## C. Describe conflicting interviews, do not mention gossip boy reliability
## D. Include only coming out, attributed to sources/gossip boy
## E. Include only coming out, in wiki voice. 
## F. Include in some other way

Note : I have neutrally notified several noticeboards and wikiprojects regarding this RFC [[User:ResultingConstant|ResultingConstant]] ([[User talk:ResultingConstant|talk]]) 21:48, 9 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Jorge I. Domínguez#rfc_6E2FFD7|Talk:Jorge I. Domínguez]] expired 2018-04-10 04:01 ===
* Id: 6E2FFD7
* User: HouseOfChange
* Date: 2018-03-11 04:00:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|829846776|BIO 829846776}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|835682041|BIO 835682041}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The subject of this article has been accused of sexual harassment, first in 1983 (after which Harvard disciplined but retained and later promoted him) and very recently, with stories emerging going back for decades alleging inappropriate behavior. Of course some of this material should be in the bio, but I have a disagreement with another editor (or possibly five, although the IP addresses are very similar) about WP:WEIGHT. On the talk page, they are sharply critical of my edits to the article.

The IPs ([[Special:Contributions/2604:2000:E016:A700:8853:2F07:A72D:96A2]], [[Special:Contributions/2604:2000:E016:A700:F81C:D427:6CB1:E49F]], [[Special:Contributions/2604:2000:E016:A700:14D7:F45B:2E06:DDDC]], [[Special:Contributions/2604:2000:E016:A700:E1FD:CB3E:641B:795B]], [[Special:Contributions/2604:2000:E016:A700:FDB2:3234:2AAA:AB32]]) have been editing this article aggressively to add all possible references for the sex scandal, including transforming one Harvard Crimson article into 3, and citing both one Newsweek article and its absolute duplicate in Yahoo. 

I think that the number of overlapping references, the paragraph they added to the header, and the accusatory tone of the Sexual harassment section, are inappropriate to WP:WEIGHT and BLP. It will be better to have one sentence at most in the header, with maybe three paragraphs in the body, including links to articles where interested people can read the detailed salacious claims against the subject. 

I am not trying to whitewash the subject. What he is accused of is reprehensible and claims against him are news. But unless I am wrong, the amount of space and detail spent describing these claims should have some balance with the amount of space the article spends describing his notability. What do others think? Thanks! [[User:HouseOfChange|HouseOfChange]] ([[User talk:HouseOfChange|talk]]) 04:00, 11 March 2018 (UTC)}}

:* Claims, Marketing and Sales: 0% error ratio<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|3}}
:* Policyholder services: 13% error ratio<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|3}}
:** According to the report, "The examiners found four complaints where New York Life failed to provide a written response to the complainant within a reasonable period of 10 working days."<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|3}}
:* Replacement file review: No problems<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|6,9}}
:* Underwriting: 0% error ratio<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|10}}
:* Claims review: 0% error ratio<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|11}}
:* Advertising and forms: 0% error ratio<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|12}}

:In addition to those areas, a review was also conducted regarding the disciplinary actions performed on agents of the company. The review found that of 11 agents disciplined, none were for "activities related to the replacement of annuities or life insurance policies".<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|13}} With regards to improving policyholder services, the examiners noted they were "satisfied that the Companies (NYLIC) have taken or will take corrective measures pursuant to the recommendations of the Report."<ref name=njlife/>{{rp|i}}

* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The lede should contain the often used altname Bcash and read: 

'''Bitcoin Cash''' (also known as '''Bcash''') is a [[cryptocurrency]].<ref name="fortunebcash">{{Cite news|url=http://fortune.com/2017/08/08/bitcoin-price-bitcoin-cash-bcash/|title=Bitcoin Just Surged to Yet Another All-Time High|last=Shen|first=Lucinda|publisher=Fortune Magazine|date=08 August 2017}}</ref><ref name="forbes">{{Cite news|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/pamelaambler/2017/08/09/the-rapid-rise-and-fall-of-bitcoin-cash/|title=The Rapid Rise And Fall Of Bitcoin Cash|last=Ambler|first=Pamela|publisher=Forbes|date=09 August 2017}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|last1=Smith|first1=Oli|title=Bitcoin price RIVAL: Cryptocurrency 'faster than bitcoin' will CHALLENGE market leaders|url=https://www.express.co.uk/finance/city/907536/cryptocurrency-bitcoin-market-leader-cash-ripple-ethereum|accessdate=1 March 2018|work=Express|date=21 January 2018}}</ref> 

[[MOS:LEADALT]] applies the following test: "significant alternative names for the topic should be mentioned in the article, usually in the first sentence or paragraph." [[WP:SOAP]] applies the following test: "An article can report objectively about such things, as long as an attempt is made to describe the topic from a neutral point of view." The following mainstream [[WP:RS]] have used the term bcash:

 “the new Bitcoin spinoff, Bitcoin Cash or “Bcash,”<ref name="fortunebcash">{{Cite news|url=http://fortune.com/2017/08/08/bitcoin-price-bitcoin-cash-bcash/|title=Bitcoin Just Surged to Yet Another All-Time High|last=Shen|first=Lucinda|publisher=Fortune Magazine|date=08 August 2017}}</ref> [[Fortune (magazine)]]

 "Bitcoin Cash, now also known as "Bcash"<ref name="forbes">{{Cite news|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/pamelaambler/2017/08/09/the-rapid-rise-and-fall-of-bitcoin-cash/|title=The Rapid Rise And Fall Of Bitcoin Cash|last=Ambler|first=Pamela|publisher=Forbes|date=09 August 2017}}</ref> [[Forbes]]

 “Aurélien Menant, founder and CEO of [[Gatecoin]], a regulated bitcoin and ethereum token exchange based in Hong Kong, says parts of the community are referring to the new token as Bcash.”<ref name="cnbc">{{Cite news|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2017/07/31/blockchain-fork-will-create-new-digital-crypto-currency-bitcoin-cash.html|title=A new digital currency is about to be created as the bitcoin blockchain is forced to split in two|last=Graham|first=Luke|publisher=CNBC|date=31 July 2017}}</ref>  [[CNBC]] 

The following industry [[WP:RS]] have used the term bcash
 "Throughout the past month, several major Bitcoin exchanges such as Bitstamp and Bitfinex have either listed or referred to Bitcoin Cash as Bcash in several instances."<ref name="CoinTelegraph">{{Cite news|url=https://cointelegraph.com/news/bitstamp-criticized-for-listing-bitcoin-cash-as-bcash-despite-community-outrage|title=Bitstamp Criticized For Listing Bitcoin Cash as Bcash, Despite Community Outrage|last=Young|first=Joseph|publisher=CoinTelegraph|date=6 December 2017}}</ref> CoinTelegraph

 "For the past couple of days, Bitcoin Cash (Bcash or BCH) was more profitable to mine than Bitcoin (BTC)."<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://bitcoinmagazine.com/articles/why-bcash-mining-shouldnt-affect-bitcoin-much-bitcoin-mining-could-ruin-bcash/|title=Why Bcash Mining Shouldn’t Affect Bitcoin Much (But Bitcoin Mining Could Ruin Bcash)|last=van Wirdum|first=Aaron|publisher=BitcoinMagazine|date=22 August 2017}}</ref> [[Bitcoin Magazine]]

The above sources demonstrate a pattern of usage of the term Bcash in both mainstream and industry publications.

'''Revised RfC on altname Bcash'''

This proposal is to add altname ([[MOS:LEADALT]]) "Bcash" to the [[Bitcoin Cash]] article with ammended text to read:  

'''Bitcoin Cash''' (also known as '''Bcash''').<ref name="fortunebcash">{{Cite news|url=http://fortune.com/2017/08/08/bitcoin-price-bitcoin-cash-bcash/|title=Bitcoin Just Surged to Yet Another All-Time High|last=Shen|first=Lucinda|publisher=Fortune Magazine|date=08 August 2017}}</ref><ref name="forbes">{{Cite news|url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/pamelaambler/2017/08/09/the-rapid-rise-and-fall-of-bitcoin-cash/|title=The Rapid Rise And Fall Of Bitcoin Cash|last=Ambler|first=Pamela|publisher=Forbes|date=09 August 2017}}</ref><ref name="cnbc">{{Cite news|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2017/07/31/blockchain-fork-will-create-new-digital-crypto-currency-bitcoin-cash.html|title=A new digital currency is about to be created as the bitcoin blockchain is forced to split in two|last=Graham|first=Luke|publisher=CNBC|date=31 July 2017}}</ref><ref name="CoinTelegraph">{{Cite news|url=https://cointelegraph.com/news/bitstamp-criticized-for-listing-bitcoin-cash-as-bcash-despite-community-outrage|title=Bitstamp Criticized For Listing Bitcoin Cash as Bcash, Despite Community Outrage|last=Young|first=Joseph|publisher=CoinTelegraph|date=6 December 2017}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://bitcoinmagazine.com/articles/why-bcash-mining-shouldnt-affect-bitcoin-much-bitcoin-mining-could-ruin-bcash/|title=Why Bcash Mining Shouldn’t Affect Bitcoin Much (But Bitcoin Mining Could Ruin Bcash)|last=van Wirdum|first=Aaron|publisher=BitcoinMagazine|date=22 August 2017}}</ref>
