=== [[Template talk:Infobox officeholder#rfc_5C96B2A|Template talk:Infobox officeholder]] expired 2018-04-14 07:01 ===
* Id: 5C96B2A
* User: Inowen
* Date: 2018-03-15 06:15:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|830678618|POLICY 830678618}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|836349549|POLICY 836349549}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Preamble: The majoritarian idea of governance often has the provision that certain majoritarian actions might be infringing on minority groups, which is to say the actions are persecutory, and therefore statutes have to be put in place to either limit majoritarian rampages, or else protect minority interests specifically. 

The RFC to remove the religion= tag from the main infobox might have come about without fair treatment of the minority opinion, and so I propose two things, that the religion= tag be restored and a guideline for its usage be written. In addition, I make the suggestion that Arbcom review the RFC in order to form guidelines to protect minority interests from majoritarian sweeps, such that as in this case, other solutions were not sought or taken. 

On the matter of the RFC and its claimed validity, the validity naturally rests entirely on the idea of it being majoritarian, and a "snow close" issue. But then atheist majoritarianism would have the problem that it would wipe away religion as a topical element from articles project wide, and that has to be prevented, by statute and guideline. 

The internet seems to have a strong showing of atheists and science-culturists, but if science culture is taking the form of an irrational cult religion, and atheism is not really a personal view but an increasingly more organized anti-religion movement, then these things need to be countered with some common sense that rejects POV movements and does honorable treatment of the human condition and the role religion has played in it. -[[User:Inowen|Inowen]] ([[User talk:Inowen|talk]]) 06:15, 15 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:List of Presidents of the United States#rfc_B1DF507|Talk:List of Presidents of the United States]] expired 2018-04-15 17:01 ===
* Id: B1DF507
* Date: 2018-03-16 16:50:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|830737294|BIO 830737294}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|830737301|HIST 830737301}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|830737304|POL 830737304}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|836577679|BIO 836577679}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|836577680|HIST 836577680}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|836577687|POL 836577687}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
 There has been an ongoing dispute over which images should be used in this list, involving experienced editors and newer editors, registered and IP users, those acting with good intentions and with those with more dubious reasons. The page was temporarily protected a few times, but has now been protected for a full year. [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States&oldid=830687047 This] is the current version of the article as of the posting of this RfC. There are 44 men representing 45 presidencies, Grover Cleveland is listed twice, using the same image. The purpose of this RfC is to establish consensus, for the images that should be included as if it's closing, and to establish that changes to images must be proposed on the talk page first and only implemented with consensus, or are otherwise immediately reverted. 
*Question 1: Do you support the current 44 images [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States&oldid=830687047 currently] listed?
**If you oppose, please indicate which image(s) you want to see changed, including a link to the replacement image(s) you are proposing and your reasoning. We'll have a straw poll for each image. 
*Question 2: Do you support that any changes to images must first be proposed on the talk page and only implemented with consensus?  
At the conclusion of this RfC, we should have a set list of 44 (or 45) images and going forward, (hopefully) have a mechanism in place to prevent any further disruption to the page. [[User:Thewolfchild|wolf]] 16:50, 16 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Consultation on the future of portals#rfc_6745CF8|Wikipedia:Consultation on the future of portals]] expired 2018-04-16 06:01 ===
* Id: 6745CF8
* Date: 2018-04-08 14:23:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|836672859|POLICY 836672859}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|836672861|PROJ 836672861}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|836672863|PROP 836672863}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|836677747|POLICY 836677747}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|836677748|PROJ 836677748}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|836677750|PROP 836677750}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
{{shortcut|WP:FPORTALS}}
On 8 April 2018, a '''[[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)|village pump proposal]]''' was submitted that proposed '''deleting Wikipedia's various [[Wikipedia:Portals|portals]]'''. The discussion quickly became very complex, involving a number of counter-proposals, and many points were repeated several times in the discussion thread. The discussion was therefore [[WP:BOLD|boldly]] closed and sequestered out to this page by [[User:Newbiepedian|Newbiepedian]] at the original suggestion of [[User:John Cline|John Cline]] in order to restructure it and provide an accessible overview to the discussion that has already taken place. This will help encourage discussion of the individual proposals.

The original discussion has been archived '''[[/RFC|here]]'''.

{{toclimit|3}}

= Background =
:''This section is not gospel, please feel free to amend if you feel anything is inaccurate or insufficiently comprehensive.''

The original proposal suggested deleting all portals.

The main arguments in '''support''' of the proposal were:
# Very few Wikipedians use portals, and therefore very few Wikipedians maintain them.
# As very few Wikipedians maintain portals, they often contain out-of-date and/or irrelevant information.
# Many portals on certain subjects are less useful as an introduction to their subject than the main article(s).
# The time Wikipedians ''do'' spend on maintaining portals would (thus) be better spent on maintaining articles.

The main arguments in '''opposition''' to the proposal were:
# Although few Wikipedians use portals, many visitors do. (See table below to that effect.)
# Blanket deletion of an entire namespace, containing a total of 185,578 pages, may have many unintended consequences &ndash; as mass deletions have done in the past.
# There are clearly some portals that ''are'' well-maintained, such as [[Portal:Current events]], and there is little reason to delete them.
# Some value would (thus) be lost by deleting all portals. An overhaul, by contrast, could potentially create value.

''' Data '''

Some users collated useful data; this is reproduced here. Please feel free to add any further relevant data to this section.

A large amount of the text already included shows that the numerous invasions were either defeated, repelled or they were just short opportunistic raids. Wikipedia guidelines on neutrality, POV, bias, due balance, etc are clear. Calling those the "conquests" is POV bias, which lends undue balance to some "wins" against the "numerous" defeats / repulsions /expulsions of muslim invaders by the native hindus/sikhs/buddhists. The contentious namespace, such as the [[Muslim conquests of the Indian subcontinent]], creates a muslim-supremacist bias. Move the article to a more non-contentious, balanced, fairer, and more accurate non-supremacist namespace, such as the [[Attempted muslim invasions of the Indian subcontinent]] or the [[Muslim invasions of the Indian subcontinent]], etc. [[Special:Contributions/202.156.182.84|202.156.182.84]] ([[User talk:202.156.182.84|talk]]) 13:55, 17 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Autoconfirmed article creation trial/Request for comment on permanent implementation#rfc_E945E64|Wikipedia:Autoconfirmed article creation trial/Request for comment on permanent implementation]] expired 2018-04-18 14:01 ===
* Id: E945E64
* User: TonyBallioni
* Date: 2018-03-19 13:39:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|831228494|POLICY 831228494}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|837061966|POLICY 837061966}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
In  April 2011, the community  reached  a [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)/Proposal to require autoconfirmed status in order to create articles|large consensus by  RfC]] for a 6  month  trial limiting  the creation  of articles in  mainspace by  non-[[WP:Autoconfirmed|autoconfirmed]] users. In June 2017 after discussions with the English Wikipedia community, the Wikimedia Foundation agreed that such a trial would be implemented. On 14 September 2017, the Wikimedia Foundation implemented the [[Wikipedia:Autoconfirmed article creation trial|Autoconfirmed article creation trial]] (commonly referred to as ACTRIAL) and it ended on 14 March 2018 after 6 months. The results of the research can be found at '''[[meta:Research:Autoconfirmed article creation trial]]''' and '''[[Wikipedia:Autoconfirmed article creation trial/Post-trial Research Report]]'''. Three of the major themes of the report were that:
#New user activity and retention is largely unaffected
#Creation of pages by new users shifted to draft space from article space
#Fewer low-quality and inappropriate  pages have been created in article space

The [[meta:Research:Autoconfirmed article creation trial|independent consultant's research]] generally shows that the concerns (hypotheses) that were raised before the trial about the restrictions having a negative impact on retention of new editors did not occur, the trial and the research conducted has received generally positive feedback. 

Following the trial, and in view of the promise to the community that the rule will not be permanently installed without a further discussion, it is proposed that as from 3 May 2018, (or sooner if a consensus is reached): 

'''Creation of new articles in the main space is restricted to accounts that have reached autoconfirmed status (four days registered and at least ten edits).'''
[[User:TonyBallioni|TonyBallioni]] ([[User talk:TonyBallioni|talk]]) 13:39, 19 March 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
The article has NPOV issues. A lot of it seems to be coming from manipulation of references, for instance:

{{tq| * “In a 2004 public release, Amnesty International stated it continues to receive reports of human rights violations carried out by the MEK against its own members.[194]” }}

The Amnesty International statement actual says the contrary, that the Iranian regime tortured a suspected MEK member.

This creates NPOV issues as the Iranian Regime considers this group one of its [https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/tehrans-futile-attempts-at-discrediting-the-cause-for-regime-change-in-iran/article/2641728 main political threats]. {{tq| * “Members who defected from the MEK and some experts say that these Mao-style self-criticism sessions are intended to enforce control over sex and marriage in the organization as a total institution.[184]” }}

Proposing cleaning up the article and removing references funded by the Iranian Regime as these will have an inevitable bias against this group. One particular editor has monopolized the article and won’t anyone edit it, so requesting feedback from neutral editors. Support / Oppose ? [[User:London Hall|London Hall]] ([[User talk:London Hall|talk]]) 13:18, 6 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Vladimir Peftiev#rfc_5569C23|Talk:Vladimir Peftiev]] expired 2018-04-23 20:01 ===
* Id: 5569C23
* User: 46.56.226.159
* Date: 2018-03-24 19:23:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|832251754|BIO 832251754}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|837914883|BIO 837914883}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This article contains coverage of EU sanctions that were brought against the article's subject, Vladimir Peftiev, and enforced from portions of 2011 through 2014. Peftiev brought legal challenge against the sanctions and in Decemeber 2014, the Council of the European Union (the same body which imposed the sanctions) voided them.  While some discussion of these facts has been present in the article since 2016, there is now a dispute as to how much coverage these events should receive in the article; recent edits have considerably expanded the coverage of the criticisms section--not just with regard to the sanctions, but also additional related allegations which have been made against Peftiev. Other editors have advocated against this additional content. The span of perspectives is reasonably captured by the following two drafts: [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vladimir_Peftiev&oldid=829311329 fleshed-out criticism section], [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vladimir_Peftiev&oldid=828504540 a more conservative criticism section].

Advocates for the minimalist approach have argued that recently added content is based on sourcing which is either unreliable or insufficient to support the new content, given the increased burden which must be met for [[WP:EXCEPTIONAL]] claims.  They further argue that, even putting the source reliability aside, some of this content may over-emphasize accusations which are [[WP:UNDUE]] under our weight policies, given the circumstances and the fact that the EU has explicitly annulled the sanctions against Peftiev.  Advocates for the inclusionist perspective disagree and find the sources both reliable and appropriate to the claims they support, and argue that the coverage of additional allegations against Peftiev (some related to the sanctions, some not) is both [[WP:DUE]] and [[WP:PROPORTION]]AL. Your input is requested on the following questions:

1) Which of the following sources are appropriate or inappropriate for use in the context they would be utilized for in [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vladimir_Peftiev&oldid=831067416 the current version of the article]? 
*[https://www.nv-online.info/2010/08/06/vladimir-peftiev-milliarder.html Narodnaja Volya]
*[https://gazetaby.com/cont/art.php?sn_nid=42797 gazetaby.com]
*[https://www.kommersant.ru/doc/1896992 Ogoniok]
*[https://charter97.org/en/news/2013/9/4/75078/ Charter97]
*[https://nn.by/?c=ar&i=61552 Nasha Niva] 
*[[Malta Today]] ([https://www.maltatoday.com.mt/business/business_news/30726/citizenship-individual-investor-programme-20131016 one], [https://www.maltatoday.com.mt/news/national/16293/foreign-ministry-issues-penalties-on-trade-with-belarus-tycoon-20120223#.WgLDYNhRWUk two], [https://www.maltatoday.com.mt/news/world/69839/belarus_dictators_bagman_vladimir_peftiev_once_a_malta_resident_named_in_bahamas_offshore_leaks#.WgLBWthRWUk three], [https://www.maltatoday.com.mt/news/national/12485/us-embassy-cables-belarus-money-man-channelled-funds-from-malta-to-dictator#.WgLDrthRWUk four], [https://www.maltatoday.com.mt/news/national/65287/panama_papers__wife_of_belarus_oligarch_in_malta_used_bvi_companies_during_eu_sanctions five])
*[http://webdoc.france24.com/inside_belarus_networks/ France24]

2) Given your perspective on question #1, which statements do you feel are unsupported and should be removed?

We apologize that this RfC does not give respondents a clearer question to !vote up or down, but your input as to the underlying issue of which sources are or are not reliable for the claims they currently support could be very useful in breaking this deadlock, thank you!

[[Special:Contributions/46.56.226.159|46.56.226.159]] ([[User talk:46.56.226.159|talk]]) 19:23, 24 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:In the news#rfc_92E5CA0|Wikipedia talk:In the news]] expired 2018-04-24 12:01 ===
* Id: 92E5CA0
* User: WTKitty
* Date: 2018-04-24 10:27:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|838007757|PROJ 838007757}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|838014093|PROJ 838014093}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
What are the parameters, purpose, and scope of in the news? and what do users want in the news to be?

This discussion is intended to be a completely open discussion where there are no "starting points". It is for everyone to give a view of what they see for In The nNews. Please do not fall back and state "this already known" or "this is obvious" or "this has already been decided" or similar that will not help with the discussions and has the potential to be seen as hostile and unconstructive. 

There are no right or wrong answers here and everything from complete reworking, to retaining the status quo, to scrapping ITN, are welcome to be discussed. These are mere suggestions and are not a list of must be discussed issues. 

Please remain civil at all times.

[[User:WTKitty|WTKitty]] ([[User talk:WTKitty|talk]]) 10:27, 24 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)#rfc_8C7D5BE|Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)]] expired 2018-04-26 03:01 ===
* Id: 8C7D5BE
* User: Lojbanist
* Date: 2018-04-06 01:15:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|834551441|PROJ 834551441}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|838290832|PROJ 838290832}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
:{{pagelinks|Wikipedia:WikiProject Stub sorting}}
:{{pagelinks|Wikipedia:WikiProject Stub sorting/Proposals}}
:{{pagelinks|Wikipedia:WikiProject Stub sorting/Criteria}}
:{{pagelinks|Wikipedia:WikiProject Stub sorting/Naming conventions}}
:{{pagelinks|Wikipedia:WikiProject Stub sorting/Discoveries}} - used to point out BOLD editors who choose to apply IAR to the WSS process
:{{pagelinks|Wikipedia:WikiProject Stub sorting/Stub types}} - '''move''' to [[Wikipedia:Template messages/Stubs]]
:{{pagelinks|Template:Stubsort}} - used to bug people who use the generic [[Template:Stub]]
:{{pagelinks|Template:Stub sort}} - same as stubsort
:{{pagelinks|Template:WPSS-cat}}
:{{pagelinks|Template:WPSS-new}}
:redundant over-specific templates - {{tl|underpopulated stub category}}, {{tl|very large stub category}}, {{tl|deprecated stub}}

Do we '''really''' need all this bureaucracy for stub templates? I don't think so. You want to create a new stub template? You have to go through WSS first. What's that, you've decided to just be bold and create the template? Too bad; it's going to TFD, where the 5 active TFDers will ignore it, causing it to be automaticallly deleted. I propose that WSS be shut down and the stub template process be made much less process-y, per the Esperanza precedent. (This was originally on MFD, but I was told to go here, despite MFD being where the dissolution of Esperanza was discussed.) '''[[User:Lojbanist|Lojbanist]]''' <sup>[[User talk:Lojbanist|remove cattle from stage]]</sup> 01:15, 6 April 2018 (UTC)}}

Sometime ago, {{Article|Fauxcest}} was merged with {{Article|Incest pornography}}. The rationale behind this was [[WP:NEO]], [[WP:POVFORK]] and that the Fauxcest article was not much bigger than the section on Fauxcest at the Incest pornography article. An IP has challenged this. The IP somewhat expanded the article, and has argued that "stepfamily is non-consanguineous" and that "we could rename [the article] to pseudo-incest." A counterargument is that that "fauxcest" mainly concerns pornography, sexual activity between step-siblings is still referred to as [[incest]], and the current version of the article contains some [[WP:Synthesis]].   

Thoughts? [[User:Flyer22 Reborn|Flyer22 Reborn]] ([[User talk:Flyer22 Reborn|talk]]) 21:50, 3 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_19E8D28|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2018-04-27 22:01 ===
* Id: 19E8D28
* User: Eggishorn
* Date: 2018-03-28 21:13:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|832958007|POLICY 832958007}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|838572931|POLICY 838572931}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
In closing the [[ Wikipedia:Arbitration/Requests/Case/Civility in infobox discussions|Civility in infobox discussions]] arbitration case, the Arbitration committee [[Wikipedia:Arbitration/Requests/Case/Civility_in_infobox_discussions#Community_discussion_recommended|recommended]] {{tq|...well-publicized community discussions be held to address whether to adopt a policy or guideline addressing what factors should weigh in favor of or against including an infobox in a given article and how those factors should be weighted.}} As an editor who has not previously been involved in favor or against infobox usage and therefore a (hopefully) neutral party, I'm opening this discussion here. [[Wikipedia:Arbitration/Requests/Case/Infoboxes#Community_discussion_recommended|A prior call for discussion]] did not clarify standards for infobox usage. That leaves two policy questions in this latest recommendation: 
#Are infoboxes necessary for articles generally
#How editors decide if infoboxes are necessary on particular articles
It seems logical to decide the first before the second. 

The spectrum of options for the first question logically runs from "infoboxes everywhere" to "infoboxes nowhere". [[Wikipedia:Arbitration/Requests/Case/Infoboxes#Use_of_infoboxes|The previous infobox Arbitration decision]], however, found that: {{tq|[t]he use of infoboxes is neither required nor prohibited for any article by site policies or guidelines.}} The extreme policy options of "every article should have an infobox" and "no article should have an infobox" are therefore not offered as options here. The spectrum of remaining options is:
*Infoboxes are used by default on most articles – removing one from an article with one requires talk page consensus
*Infoboxes are used by default on broad class(es) of articles (e.g., biographies, biological species, etc.) – removing one from an article with one requires talk page consensus (Note: the obverse is therefore also true, articles not in the defined class(es) by default omit infoboxes.) 
<s>*Infoboxes are used by default on some more-restricted subset(s) of articles (e.g., music biographies, invertebrate species, etc.) – removing one from an article with one requires talk page consensus (Note: the obverse is therefore also true, articles not in the defined subset(s) by default omit infoboxes.)</s>
*Infoboxes are neither used by default nor omitted by default – adding one to an article without one or removing one from an article with one requires talk page consensus
*<s>Infoboxes are omitted by default on some more-restricted subset(s) of articles (e.g., music biographies, invertebrate species, etc.) – adding one to an article without one requires talk page consensus (Note: the obverse is therefore also true, articles not in the defined subset(s) by default include infoboxes.)</s>
*<s>Infoboxes are omitted by default on broad class(es) of articles (e.g., biographies, biological species, etc.) – adding one to an article without one requires talk page consensus (Note: the obverse is therefore also true, articles not in the defined class(es) by default include infoboxes.)</s>
*Infoboxes are omitted by default on most articles – adding one to an article without one requires talk page consensus 
Wikiprojects would be the most logical place to determine which articles come under the "broad classes" and "some more-restricted subset" options, where active projects exist.

'''''Request to !voters:''''' To assist the future closers of this RfC in assessing consensus on so many options, it is requested that editors ''only'' place a '''support''' !vote in the subsection below that most closely aligns with their preferred option.  '''Oppose''' !votes are ''not necessary'' and should be assumed for the remaining other options. I recognize that this "support only one option" request eliminates nuanced views but this is by design.  Previous discussions have not yielded much clarity, so clarity is preferred here over nuance.  Discussions to determine the exact parameters of the selected option, as well as question #2 listed above, will be presented later. Thank you in advance for your help. [[User:Eggishorn|Eggishorn]] [[User talk:Eggishorn|(talk)]] [[Special:Contributions/Eggishorn|(contrib)]] 21:13, 28 March 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Apache OpenOffice#rfc_E65C227|Talk:Apache OpenOffice]] expired 2018-05-03 18:01 ===
* Id: E65C227
* User: Walter Görlitz
* Date: 2018-04-03 17:39:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|834170505|SCI 834170505}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|839478522|SCI 839478522}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Request for comments. What should the 'development status' parameter be set to in the article's infobox.
:'''A''' - Moribund
:'''B''' - Low activity
:'''C''' - Stalled
:'''D''' - Slowed
:'''E''' - <empty> (indicating the project is Active per [[Template:Infobox software]])
:'''F''' - <something else>

The discussion was getting long and it needed a vertical break. While doing this, I think it would be an appropriate time to ask about suggested options.

To summarize, the documentation seems to only offer the option of "stalled" for us, since the other options (planned, unmaintained, discontinued, abandonware) are not appropriate. It is by definition, not under active development. Two additional options are "low activity" and keeping at "Moribund". I prefer the current option and my next choice would be low activity, and then stalled, but that doesn't accurately represent its development status. [[User:Walter Görlitz|Walter Görlitz]] ([[User talk:Walter Görlitz|talk]]) 17:39, 3 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Neo-Nazism#rfc_6E1E58D|Talk:Neo-Nazism]] expired 2018-05-04 02:01 ===
* Id: 6E1E58D
* User: Beyond My Ken
* Date: 2018-04-04 01:42:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|834124796|HIST 834124796}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|834124797|POL 834124797}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|839532685|HIST 839532685}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|839532687|POL 839532687}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The opening sentence of this article used to read<blockquote>Neo-Nazism consists of post-World War II militant social or political movements seeking to revive the ideology of Nazism.</blockquote> On 24 March, [[User:LightandDark2000]] added the words "and implement" to the sentence, so that it read<blockquote>Neo-Nazism consists of post-World War II militant social or political movements seeking to revive and implement the ideology of Nazism.</blockquote>The purpose of this RfC is to determine whether "and implement" &ndash; or other equivalent or near-equivalent phrases, such as "and establish" or "and put into effect" &ndash; should be kept in the opening sentence, or if it should be reverted to the original version. [[User:Beyond My Ken|Beyond My Ken]] ([[User talk:Beyond My Ken|talk]]) 01:42, 4 April 2018 (UTC)}}

'''An editor has added [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tattoo&type=revision&diff=834211972&oldid=834073230 tattooage] to the article several times after being reverted by myself and another editor. === [[Wikipedia:Wikidata/2018 Infobox RfC#rfc_2900C5D|Wikipedia:Wikidata/2018 Infobox RfC]] expired 2018-05-06 21:01 ===
* Id: 2900C5D
* Date: 2018-04-06 20:49:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|835146363|POLICY 835146363}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|835146364|TECH 835146364}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|839960706|POLICY 839960706}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|839960708|TECH 839960708}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Since the [[Wikipedia:Requests for comment/Wikidata Phase 2|2013 RfC on Wikidata Phase 2]], using Wikidata in infoboxes has gone from the concept stage to more extensive mainspace experimental implementations. This had led to some controversies: some editors have been converting infoboxes to use Wikidata, believing use of Wikidata brings significant benefits, while other editors have been removing Wikidata from infoboxes, believing use of Wikidata brings significant problems. The opposing efforts are counterproductive. It is time to ask the broader Wikipedia editor community where to take it from here. 20:49, 6 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Heldeep Records#rfc_4654632|Talk:Heldeep Records]] expired 2018-05-06 22:01 ===
* Id: 4654632
* Date: 2018-05-06 10:19:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|839890668|MEDIA 839890668}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|839968344|MEDIA 839968344}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
There is no significant in-depth coverage for this record label and AFD resulted in "keep because redirect/merge can be discussed on talk". I propose to redirect the article to the label's owner Oliver Heldens, who is a notable DJ and musician. His label has no notability on its own and [[WP:NOTINHERITED|notability is not inherited]].

=== [[Wikipedia:Requests for comment/Event coordinator proposal#rfc_A7A79FB|Wikipedia:Requests for comment/Event coordinator proposal]] expired 2018-05-08 14:01 ===
* Id: A7A79FB
* User: TonyBallioni
* Date: 2018-04-18 14:24:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|837071177|PROP 837071177}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|840221459|PROP 840221459}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
{{shortcut|WP:RFC/ECP}}
One of the points of feedback on the recent [[Wikipedia:Autoconfirmed article creation trial|autoconfirmed account creation trial]] has been that some Wikimedians who work in GLAM and outreach activities to conduct edit-a-thons and trainings felt that the trial negatively impacted their ability to bring in new members of the Wikimedia community. In order to help meet these concerns, I am proposing that a new <code>eventcoordinator</code> user permission be created with the following abilities and guidelines for use and granting:
#The {{code|eventcoordinator}} user group will receive the ability to temporarily add {{code|+confirmed}} to newly created accounts, and will also receive the {{code|(noratelimit)}} right in order to help with account creation. This will allow the Confirmed new accounts to create mainspace pages without waiting 4 days and 10 edits and allow the creation of many new accounts from the same IP address.
#Event coordinators should set the expiry time of the confirmed user right to no more than ten days from the time it is granted. 
#Administrators should only permanently grant the {{code|eventcoordinator}} user right to editors with an established record of editing on Wikipedia. Administrators may at their discretion temporarily grant the permission to editors who are organizing outreach events but do not have significant experience on Wikipedia. Users who have not edited in over a year may have the permission removed for inactivity.
#Event coordinators should only confirm users who actually participate in an outreach event.

[[User:TonyBallioni|TonyBallioni]] ([[User talk:TonyBallioni|talk]]) 14:24, 18 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:CSA Steaua Bucure?ti (football)#rfc_1714458|Talk:CSA Steaua Bucure?ti (football)]] expired 2018-05-08 19:01 ===
* Id: 1714458
* User: 8Dodo8
* Date: 2018-04-08 18:08:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|835443496|POL 835443496}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|835443501|SOC 835443501}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|840259897|POL 840259897}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|840259901|SOC 840259901}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
[[FC Steaua București]], the most notable football club from Romania, lost its name and logo following some Romanian Justice Court decisions and became "Fotbal Club FCSB" in early 2017.<ref name="steaua_change_name_to_fcsb">{{cite web|url= http://theworldgame.sbs.com.au/article/2017/03/31/steaua-bucharest-change-name-fc-fcsb|title=Steaua Bucharest change name to FC FCSB|publisher=[[Special Broadcasting Service]]|date=31 March 2017|accessdate=25 April 2017}}</ref> Meanwhile, the Romanian Army, which had owned the club until 1998 and is still in charge of several sport clubs, "restarted" its football department ([[CSA Steaua București (football)]]) in the summer of that year and commenced play in the fourth league.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.prosport.ro/fotbal-intern/si-au-pus-antrenor-acum-aduc-jucatorii-lacatus-pana-la-jumatatea-lunii-iulie-vrem-sa-incepem-pregatirea-cu-25-26-de-jucatori-16212918|title=Şi-au pus antrenor, acum aduc jucătorii. Lăcătuş: "Până la jumătatea lunii iulie, vrem să începem pregătirea cu 25-26 de jucători"|trans-title=They named a head coach, now they bring players. Lăcătuş: "Until mid-July, we wish to start the training with 25-26 players"|language=Romanian|publisher=[[Pro Sport]]|date=29 March 2017|accessdate=29 March 2017}}</ref>

As of now, FCSB is credited as the successor of FC Steaua by both [[UEFA]] and the Romanian Professional League (LPF), owning 26 domestic titles and 1 [[UEFA Champions League]], among others. This is very easy to verify by checking FCSB's UEFA.com profile.<ref name=uefa>{{cite web|url=https://www.uefa.com/teamsandplayers/teams/club=50065/profile/index.html|title=Profile: Fotbal Club FCSB|publisher=UEFA.com|date=|access-date=1 November 2017}}</ref> However, the fans of the fourth league club CSA Steaua claim that their club has 21 league trophies and the UCL from 1989, which has not been confirmed by any reliable source (UEFA, LPF or the Romanian Justice Court). Currently, they have only won the right to use the "Steaua" brand, and the process about the honours has been only been opened in December 2017 and it will take several years to resolve, probably.<ref name="honours">{{cite web|url=http://www.ziare.com/fcsb/stiri-fcsb/csa-steaua-a-dat-in-judecata-fcsb-talpan-vrea-sa-l-lase-pe-becali-si-fara-palmaresul-stelei-1495100|title=CSA Steaua a dat in judecata FCSB: Iata ce scrie in dosarul depus la Tribunalul Bucuresti|trans-title=CSA Steaua sued FCSB: See what is written in the file submitted at the Justice Court of Bucharest|publisher=Ziare|date=29 December 2017|accessdate=8 April 2017}}</ref>

Despite this, [[User:TPTB]] called me a "vandal" when I added this sentence on the CSA Steaua page: "''However, according to UEFA, FCSB is the successor of Steaua and they hold the records of the former club, including the European Champions Cup won in 1986.''" He also changed the link from [[Template:UEFA Champions League winners]] and it seems nobody is doing anything to resolve this issue for more than one year.

I suggest removing the honours of the club on this article and most of its content which is copy-pasted from FC Steaua Bucuresti, until either a Court Decision or UEFA shows that FCSB lost its right to have the records of Steaua. User:TPTB argues that CSA also won the honours in Court, but this is false:
*The files for CSA to gain the honours have been submitted at the Court only in December 2017, as I said earlier<ref name="honours"/>
*The links he provides only contain statements made by people affiliated with CSA, not any OFFICIAL decisions. 
He also called me a "liar" on multiple occasions for trying to resolve this issue.
[[User:8Dodo8|8Dodo8]] ([[User talk:8Dodo8|talk]] '''·''' [[Special:Contribs/8Dodo8|contribs]]) 18:08, 8 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Bill Shorten#rfc_B90F11D|Talk:Bill Shorten]] expired 2018-05-11 04:01 ===
* Id: B90F11D
* Date: 2018-04-11 03:57:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|835847301|BIO 835847301}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|840635360|BIO 840635360}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
There has been much debate on this talk page about the inclusion of a rape allegation. Does this proposed addition address it in a way that is consistent with Wikipedia's guidelines, especially WP:BLP and WP:UNDUE? 

{{talkquote|In 2013 a woman, known as Kathy, accused Shorten of having raped her during a 1986 Young Labor camp in Portarlington when she was 16 and he was 19.<ref name="Hurley">{{cite news|last1=Hurley|first1=David|title=Woman who accuses Opposition Leader Bill Shorten of rape says police failed her|url=http://www.heraldsun.com.au/news/woman-who-accuses-opposition-leader-bill-shorten-of-rape-says-police-failed-her/news-story/a92bad447392ff36830daa5ef2f8971e|work=Herald Sun|date=1 October 2014|location=Melbourne, Vic.}}</ref><ref name="Marr">{{cite news|last1=Marr|first1=David|title=Bill Shorten: the man in the machine|url=https://www.smh.com.au/lifestyle/the-man-in-the-machine-20160512-gotfb2.html|work=The Sydney Morning Herald|date=12 May 2016}}</ref> Rumours of the allegation proliferated "for some time" in Canberra and online before it became public.{{refn|name=Marr}}<ref name="Lewis">{{cite news|last1=Lewis|first1=Steve|title=Shorten’s gamble on rape claims|url=https://thenewdaily.com.au/news/national/2014/08/21/bill-shorten-rape-allegations/|work=The New Daily|location=Melbourne, Vic.|date=21 August 2014}}</ref> Victoria Police interviewed Shorten and various witnesses over a ten month period and decided not to lodge charges when the DPP advised "there was no reasonable prospect of conviction" based on the evidence collected.<ref name="Senior">{{cite news|title=Senior Labor Party figure will not face criminal charges over alleged rape in 1980s|url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/2014-08-21/no-charges-for-labor-figure-over-alleged-rape-in-1980s/5685846|work=ABC News|date=21 August 2014}}</ref> Afterward, Shorten said the allegation was "untrue and abhorrent".<ref name="Griffiths">{{cite news|last1=Griffiths|first1=Emma|title=Bill Shorten speaks out after 1980s rape allegation case dropped|url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/2014-08-21/bill-shorten-says-name-cleared-over-rape-allegation/5687172|work=ABC News|date=21 August 2014}}</ref> According to journalist and Shorten biographer, [[David Marr (journalist)|David Marr]], Kathy's "allegation [was] detailed" but he also noted her "confusion and distress".{{refn|name=Marr}} In November 2014, Kathy's lawyer revealed that she had not consulted a lawyer about the rape allegation until after the police closed their investigation.<ref name="Merritt">{{cite news|last1=Merritt|first1=Chris|title=Bill Shorten faces bid to revisit sex claim|url=https://www.theaustralian.com.au/national-affairs/bill-shorten-faces-bid-to-revisit-sex-claim/news-story/6621d8e7906a412d012ca81d4eb21f86|work=The Australian|date=2 November 2014|subscription=yes}}</ref>{{reflist}}}}

My view: BLP rules allow for the publication of an alleged event that is based on uncontentious and well sourced material that is cited and easily verified and where no undue weight is placed on it. As such, it was positioned at the bottom of the wiki, it was made clear that it was an allegation, the sources were cited with links, the sources were reputable, the story lasted longer than a week (one year, but also a 2015-16 biography) and the subject (Shorten) himself addressed the allegations, as well as the police, the alleged victim and Prime Minister [[Malcolm Turnbull]]. Many wiki pages of living persons discuss allegations: [[Geoffrey Rush]], [[Kevin Spacey]], [[Don Burke]] and [[Harvey Weinstein]] to name a few. [[User:Jack bulldog 2012]] 03:57, 11 April 2018 (UTC)}}

Version 1:  '''Adolescence''' ({{etymology|la|adolescere|to grow up}})<ref name="MacmillanDictionaryforStudents">''Macmillan Dictionary for Students'' Macmillan, Pan Ltd. (1981), page 14, 456. Retrieved 2010-7-15.</ref> is a transitional stage of [[Developmental biology|physical]] and [[psychological]] [[Human development (biology)|development]] that generally occurs during the period from [[puberty]] to legal adulthood ([[age of majority]]).<ref name=MacmillanDictionaryforStudents/><ref name="Adolescence">{{cite web|title=Adolescence|publisher=''[[Merriam-Webster]]''|accessdate=May 9, 2012|url=http://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/adolescence}}</ref><ref name="nlm.nih.gov">{{Cite news|title=Puberty and adolescence|publisher=[[MedlinePlus]]|accessdate=July 22, 2014|archivedate=April 3, 2013|url=https://www.nlm.nih.gov/medlineplus/ency/article/001950.htm|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130403080324/https://www.nlm.nih.gov/medlineplus/ency/article/001950.htm}}</ref> 

Version 2: 
'''Adolescence''' ({{etymology|la|adolescere|to grow up}})<ref name="MacmillanDictionaryforStudents">''Macmillan Dictionary for Students'' Macmillan, Pan Ltd. (1981), page 14, 456. Retrieved 2010-7-15.</ref> is a transitional stage, which includes [[Developmental biology|physical]] and [[psychological]] [[Human development (biology)|development]], that generally occurs during the period from the beginning of [[puberty]] to legal adulthood ([[age of majority]]).<ref name=MacmillanDictionaryforStudents/><ref name="Adolescence">{{cite web|title=Adolescence|publisher=''[[Merriam-Webster]]''|accessdate=May 9, 2012|url=http://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/adolescence}}</ref><ref name="nlm.nih.gov">{{Cite news|title=Puberty and adolescence|publisher=[[MedlinePlus]]|accessdate=July 22, 2014|archivedate=April 3, 2013|url=https://www.nlm.nih.gov/medlineplus/ency/article/001950.htm|archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20130403080324/https://www.nlm.nih.gov/medlineplus/ency/article/001950.htm}}</ref> 

'''Note''': The difference between the versions are the commas, and the "which includes" and "the beginning of" wording. [[User:Flyer22 Reborn|Flyer22 Reborn]] ([[User talk:Flyer22 Reborn|talk]]) 16:50, 12 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Syria#rfc_DD6EE60|Talk:Syria]] expired 2018-05-15 14:01 ===
* Id: DD6EE60
* User: Greyshark09
* Date: 2018-04-15 13:43:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|836603879|HIST 836603879}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|836603884|POL 836603884}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|841379578|HIST 841379578}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|841379582|POL 841379582}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I would like to ask editors whether this article lead should include Ba'athist Syria as one of the common names of the Syrian Arab Republic. Currently it is still a consensus that [[Syria]] refers to the [[Syrian Arab Republic]], which is a unitary geopolitical entity (state) ruled by the al-Assad dynasty on behalf of the [[Ba'ath Party (Syrian-dominated faction)|Syria-based Ba'ath Party]], which is ruling Syrian Arab Republic since the 1963 coup d'etat. In a very similar case for Iraq during the Ba'athist period 1968-2003 the country article is named [[Ba'athist Iraq]]. Furthermore, ''Ba'athist Syria'' is a very common term in media and scholar literature to refer to the Ba'ath ruled Syrian Arab Republic's territory, population and military (see [https://books.google.co.il/books?id=l5NODwAAQBAJ&pg=PP31&lpg=PP31&dq=%22ba%27athist+syria%22&source=bl&ots=5Fz2fqmty3&sig=I58Igyfq6CFBwjs0BITfAfuPUNo&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwij0evLs7zaAhVGWCwKHaJXB4E4ChDoAQgmMAA#v=onepage&q=%22ba'athist%20syria%22&f=false Quicksilver War: Syria, Iraq and the Spiral of Conflict 2018],[https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1057%2F9781137397720_4 Class and Capitalism in Syria 2016],[https://books.google.co.il/books?id=PJGd5wZBNH0C&pg=PA72&lpg=PA72&dq=%22ba%27athist+syria%22&source=bl&ots=ycPGEOdR0t&sig=U2FDLhr9xMn8o38Zhic6RJxKx10&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwi7uY6stLzaAhVSJ1AKHYYXArQ4FBDoAQgsMAE#v=onepage&q=%22ba'athist%20syria%22&f=false Everyday Arab Identity: The Daily Reproduction of the Arab World 2013],[https://books.google.co.il/books?id=J3PsAb1uV94C&pg=PA148&lpg=PA148&dq=%22ba%27athist+syria%22&source=bl&ots=5rRle7wlg1&sig=1kBXELb3nGMdNXax3h-HMNS7lW0&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwij0evLs7zaAhVGWCwKHaJXB4E4ChDoAQhAMAU#v=onepage&q=%22ba'athist%20syria%22&f=false Greater Syria: The History of an Ambition 1992]), to differentiate it from pre-1963 Syrian Republic and from other modern Syrian entities of the Syrian Civil War, such as [[North Syria Federation]] and [[Syrian Opposition]] (rebel members also often use ''Syrian Arab Republic'' as self-designated descriptory term). Please comment whether you think ''Ba'athist Syria'' should or should not be included in lead section per [[WP:COMMONNAME]] and whether it should be bolded or not.[[User:Greyshark09|'''''GreyShark''''']] ([[User talk:Greyshark09|''dibra'']]) 13:43, 15 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:AfriForum#rfc_081C8E3|Talk:AfriForum]] expired 2018-05-15 19:01 ===
* Id: 081C8E3
* User: Classical liberal za
* Date: 2018-05-14 13:40:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:

* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
{{strike|Certain editors of this page have taken to altering Afriforum's categorisation from that of a civil rights organisation to a white nationalist organisation. Please note the following:
# Afriforum quite clearly defines itself as follows "AfriForum is a non-governmental organisation, registered as a non-profit company, with the aim of protecting the rights of minorities."<ref>{{cite web|title=About AfriForum - AfriForum|url=https://www.afriforum.co.za/about/about-afriforum/|website=AfriForum|accessdate=14 May 2018}}</ref>
# Furthermore, the [[South African Human Rights Commission]] has referred to Afriforum as a civil rights organisation "as well as “certain actions” of civil rights organisation group Afriforum"<ref>{{cite web|title=Human Rights Commission receives complaints against UP, Afriforum|url=https://www.sahrc.org.za/index.php/sahrc-media/news/item/470-human-rights-commission-receives-complaints-against-up-afriforum|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en-gb}}</ref>
Prominent local media sources commonly refer to Afriforum as a civil rights organisation:
# SABC (The South African state broadcaster): "The Helen Suzman Foundation and civil rights organisation AfriForum have welcomed President Cyril Ramaphosa’s..." <ref>{{cite web|title=Civil rights groups welcome Ramaphosa's amendment on State Capture - SABC News - Breaking news, special reports, world, business, sport coverage of all South African current events. Africa's news leader.|url=http://www.sabcnews.com/sabcnews/civil-rights-groups-welcome-ramaphosas-amendment-state-capture/|website=SABC News - Breaking news, special reports, world, business, sport coverage of all South African current events. Africa's news leader.|accessdate=14 May 2018|date=24 March 2018}}</ref>
# ENCA: "Civil rights group AfriForum has launched a national campaign to test the quality of the country's drinking water." <ref>{{cite web|title=AfriForum's water campaign 'opportunistic'|url=https://www.enca.com/south-africa/afriforums-water-campaign-branded-opportunistic|website=www.enca.com|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
# News24: "Civil rights organisation AfriForum says while Vicki Momberg's remarks were..." <ref>{{cite web|title=Momberg's sentence confirms double standards in SA – AfriForum|url=https://www.news24.com/SouthAfrica/News/mombergs-sentence-confirms-double-standards-in-sa-afriforum-20180328|website=News24|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
# PoliticsWeb: "The civil rights organisation AfriForum today announced that its..." <ref>{{cite web|title=AfriForum tackles Canadian mining company - POLITICS {{!}} Politicsweb|url=http://www.politicsweb.co.za/politics/afriforum-tackles-canadian-mining-company|website=www.politicsweb.co.za|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
# The Mail & Guardian: "A civil rights organisation has laid a charge with the world’s..." <ref>{{cite web|last1=Reporter|first1=Staff|title=Rights group takes up Semenya race issue|url=https://mg.co.za/article/2009-08-31-rights-group-takes-up-semenya-race-issue|website=The M&G Online|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>

# The Times Live: "The National Prosecuting Authority (NPA) says charges civil rights group AfriForum laid..." <ref>{{cite web|title=NPA hits back at AfriForum|url=https://www.timeslive.co.za/news/south-africa/2018-04-11-npa-hits-back-at-afriforum/|accessdate=14 May 2018}}</ref>

# The South African: "Civil rights organisation, AfriForum has accused Volkswagen South Africa..." <ref>{{cite web|last1=Breakfast|first1=Siviwe|title=AfriForum take aim at Volkswagen over "racist policy"|url=https://www.thesouthafrican.com/afriforum-take-aim-at-volkswagen-over-racist-policy/|website=The South African|date=8 May 2018}}</ref>

# The Independent Online: "...the civil rights group said on Tuesday." <ref>{{cite web|title=AfriForum gears up to tackle Grace Mugabe in court {{!}} IOL News|url=https://www.iol.co.za/news/south-africa/afriforum-gears-up-to-tackle-grace-mugabe-in-court-14844203|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>

# News24: "Civil rights group AfriForum on Wednesday opened..." <ref>{{cite web|title=AfriForum opens cases against social media abusers|url=https://www.news24.com/SouthAfrica/News/AfriForum-opens-cases-against-social-media-abusers-20150318|website=News24|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
# The New Age: "The civil rights organisation, AfriForum says..." <ref>{{cite web|title=We are coming for you Julius Malema: AfriForum {{!}} Afro Voice|url=http://www.thenewage.co.za/we-are-coming-for-you-julius-malema-afriforum/|website=Afro Voice|accessdate=14 May 2018}}</ref>
# News24: "Civil rights organisation AfriForum on Thursday..." <ref>{{cite web|title=AfriForum condemns 'racist' Dan Roodt|url=https://www.news24.com/SouthAfrica/News/AfriForum-condemns-racist-Dan-Roodt-20141113|website=News24|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
# The Citizen: "Advocate Gerrie Nel, of civil rights watchdog AfriForum, has announced..." <ref>{{cite web|last1=Keppler|first1=Virginia|title=Nel to fight for Engels despite being ‘offered money’ to drop charges|url=https://citizen.co.za/news/south-africa/1616492/gerrie-nel-to-represent-gabriella-engels-despite-an-alleged-money-offer-to-drop-charges/|website=The Citizen|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
Furthermore, Afriforum has:
# Slammed Afrikaner racist and white nationalist Dan Roodt: "AfriForum condemned Roodt, saying that the organisation believes in mutual recognition and respect between South African communities." <ref>{{cite web|title=AfriForum slams Dan Roodt as racist|url=http://news.iafrica.com/sa/970877.html|website=iAfrica.com|accessdate=14 May 2018}}</ref>
# Taken on the case of Gabriella Engels, a Black African lady who was allegedly assaulted by then Zimbabwean President Robert Mugabe's wife Grace Mugabe, who was subsequently granted diplomatic immunity by the South African government. Afriforum has fought to have Mugabe's diplomatic immunity overturned so that Mugabe can be prosecuted for her alleged assault on Engels. <ref>{{cite web|last1=Keppler|first1=Virginia|title=Nel to fight for Engels despite being ‘offered money’ to drop charges|url=https://citizen.co.za/news/south-africa/1616492/gerrie-nel-to-represent-gabriella-engels-despite-an-alleged-money-offer-to-drop-charges/|website=The Citizen|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
# Taken on the case of the Ndebele Vaaltyn tribe, a Black African tribe who has brought criminal charges against a Canadian mining company. Afriforum stated "AfriForum was approached in March 2017 by members of the tribe because they perceive that Ivanplats may have enjoyed unjustified protection by government officials. We are considering a private prosecution to ensure equality before the law and that the rule of law prevails" and "It is one of AfriForum’s core values to promote and uphold mutual respect and recognition between communities. The Private Prosecution Unit, in line with its declaration to address selective prosecutions and those people or institutions that are sheltered from prosecution, had no hesitation to take steps to ensure that the Ndebele Vaaltyn Tribe is not treated unjustly by a failure to address the alleged unlawful actions" <ref>{{cite web|title=AfriForum tackles Canadian mining company - POLITICS {{!}} Politicsweb|url=http://www.politicsweb.co.za/politics/afriforum-tackles-canadian-mining-company|website=www.politicsweb.co.za|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
# "asked the IAAF to take strong action against those responsible for disclosing the information about the gender testing which caused the violation of Semenya's privacy and human dignity." with regards to Black African female athlete [[Caster Semenya]], who was forced to undergo the humiliation of gender-testing in 2009.<ref>{{cite web|title=ASA faces race charge|url=https://www.sport24.co.za/OtherSport/ASA-faces-race-charge-20090831-2|website=News24|accessdate=14 May 2018|language=en}}</ref>
Given the above, I strongly disagree with the assertation that Afriforum is a 'white nationalist' organisation and would greatly appreciate the input of other editors so that a firm consensus can be reached and this issue can be resolved.}} [[User:Classical liberal za|Classical liberal za]] ([[User talk:Classical liberal za|talk]]) 13:40, 14 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Dana Loesch#rfc_6E1F9B9|Talk:Dana Loesch]] expired 2018-05-16 03:01 ===
* Id: 6E1F9B9
* User: Hodgdon&#39;s secret garden
* Date: 2018-05-05 22:35:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|839826645|BIO 839826645}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|839826648|POL 839826648}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|839826649|SOC 839826649}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|841477397|BIO 841477397}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|841477399|POL 841477399}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|841477400|SOC 841477400}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
 Per [[MOS:LEADIMAGE]] ("The lead image is perhaps the first thing to catch the reader's eye, so avoid lead images that readers would not expect to see there. Unlike other content beyond the lead, the lead image should be chosen with these considerations in mind. Advice on selecting a lead image includes: Lead images should be natural and appropriate representations......"), w rgd the image currently in the blp's infobox, it doesn't IMHO seem so very bad. Perhaps the look is not uncharacteristic of the subject. I don't know. Granted: No type glamor shot, if avoidable, should be resorted to. An encyclopedia isn't intended to be promotional (''Cf.'' [[wp:Publicity photos]] and see eg [http://patterico.com/2014/06/13/judging-a-book-by-its-cover/ the subject's most recent bookjacket design: nothing akin to this]). Maybe a shot like the one currently in the infobox might be the most appropriate; Ms. Loesch appears to be captured grimacing in it, its having been chosen with a rationale similar to that for the oft editorial choice of the iconic snapshot of Winston Churchill: a candid shot that seems iconographically apropos given the subject's public persona? Hmm: Maybe this one of Loesch wouldn't be out of place in heroic statuary, sculpted in some earlier era...representing the noble American Indian princess, emoting in contempt at the desecration of her people's lands; but, I digress. Were the shot chosen because it was believed unflattering to its subject, that would be a shame, however, IMHO (see wp:NPOV). Here are some choices available at Wikimedia Commons--> [https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Dana_Loesch gallery]).--[[User:Hodgdon&#39;s secret garden|Hodgdon&#39;s secret garden]] ([[User talk:Hodgdon&#39;s secret garden|talk]]) 22:35, 5 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Categorization#rfc_53D03DF|Wikipedia talk:Categorization]] expired 2018-05-17 16:01 ===
* Id: 53D03DF
* User: 46.211.1.121
* Date: 2018-04-17 15:16:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|836911302|TECH 836911302}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|841716783|TECH 841716783}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
In the last months, user The Transhumanist has changed the [[WP:SORTKEY]] for many outline articles from "asterisk" to "space". For example, see here: [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Outline_of_mining&diff=prev&oldid=827522284] [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Outline_of_water&type=revision&diff=827523483&oldid=827482008], and many similar edits were made by him, see list [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Contributions&offset=20180225235959&limit=500&contribs=user&target=The+Transhumanist&namespace=&tagfilter=&start=2018-02-25&end=2018-02-25]. Note, "Outline of mining" is not a main article for {{category|Mining}}. Only [[Mining]] is a main article for this category. The articles typically called "History of X" ("Types of X", "List of X", "Outline of X") should be categorized with asterisk, per [[WP:SORTKEY]]. 

From [[WP:SORTKEY]]: ''The main article/s of a category, if existent, should get sorted with a space as key so that it/they appear at the very top of the category. Example: <code><nowiki>[[Category:Example| ]]</nowiki></code> Those articles are typically homonymous or at least synonymous to their category. Furthermore other general articles that are highly relevant to the category should be sorted with an asterisk as key so that they also appear at the top of a category but beneath the main article/s. Example: <code><nowiki>[[Category:Example|*]]</nowiki></code> Those articles are typically called "History of example", "Types of example", "List of example" or similar''.

I think, it's a very bad situation when "Outline of X" is located '''above''' the main "X" article in the related category. See {{Category|Wine}} for example, [[Outline of wine]] is located above [[Wine]]. The readers want to see the main article first, not "outline" of something else, so space as a sortkey should be used for only one main article (in most cases). I ask to restore the correct categorization with "asterisk" for all outline articles. [[Special:Contributions/46.211.1.121|46.211.1.121]] ([[User talk:46.211.1.121|talk]]) 15:16, 17 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Minarchism#rfc_2D9B40E|Talk:Minarchism]] expired 2018-05-18 15:01 ===
* Id: 2D9B40E
* User: BrendonTheWizard
* Date: 2018-04-18 14:44:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|837071174|POL 837071174}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|841859858|POL 841859858}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
adding new RfC template per original post by User:Daask (his nomination quote is below; I added to RfC due to only a few participants in this discussion since it was started in December)

I suggest this article be merged with [[Night-watchman state]]. I see that this has been proposed before in 2011 ([[Talk:Night-watchman_state#Why_is_this_separate_from_minarchism?|here]] and [[Talk:Night-watchman_state#Merger_Proposal|here]]), where they were distinguished between an article on a kind of state and the political philosophy which advocates for this state. I am unimpressed by this distinction.</br>
In my opinion, political philosophies are only worthy of their own articles when they become broader movements with multiple policies, reforms, or structures for which they advocate. [[Libertarianism]], [[Communism]], [[Anarchism]], and [[Socialism]] are good examples of this. Minarchism is nothing more or less than the theory and advocacy of the night-watchman state. It has no additional policies, reforms, or structures beyond this one concept. Accordingly, it seems only appropriate to merge.</br>
What do others think?

[[User:BrendonTheWizard|BrendonTheWizard]] ([[User talk:BrendonTheWizard|talk]]) 14:44, 18 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Campaign Against Antisemitism#rfc_BD07C53|Talk:Campaign Against Antisemitism]] expired 2018-05-18 18:01 ===
* Id: BD07C53
* Date: 2018-05-18 07:27:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|841817360|UNSORTED 841817360}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|841883315|UNSORTED 841883315}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
CAA brought a highly unusual private prosecution against Alison Chabloz. Ms Chabloz disputes the inclusion and characterisation of this content, specifically: she disputes that she is accused of antisemitic acts but instead the charges relate to "grossly offensive" words, stating that "{{tq|Wikipedia is supposedly independent of mainstream media. What's the point of an independent outlet that simply parrots mainstream soundbites?
}}" and denigrating the coverage as {{tq|moronic mainstream media articles}}; she asserts that she should be described as a musician not a blogger, and that the term blogger is a deliberate insult; she insists that she should be called a "holocaust revisionist" not a "holocaust denier". The following questions appear to be germane:
# Should the private prosecution be included?
# Should the target of the prosecution be described as a "blogger" per [http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-derbyshire-43321482 Blogger claims "no proof" gas chambers killed Jewish people] (BBC), [https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/blogger-alison-chabloz-sings-along-to-antisemitic-song-survivors-in-court-x5l0k7m7d Blogger Alison Chabloz sings along to antisemitic song (((Survivors))) in court] (The Times), [http://www.itv.com/news/2018-01-11/blogger-mocked-anne-frank-and-holocaust-survivors-court-told/ Blogger 'mocked Anne Frank and Holocaust survivors', court told] (ITV)?
# Should the target of the prosecution be characterised as antisemitic, per [http://courtnewsuk.co.uk/judge-considering-verdict-on-antisemitic-songwriter/ Court News] and the other RS listed above?
# Should the target of the prosecution be characterised as a [[holocaust revisionist]], [http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-derbyshire-42637888 'Holocaust revisionist'] in scare quotes as per the BBC, or a [[holocaust denier]]?
# Should the target of the prosecution be named, as per [https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/blogger-alison-chabloz-sings-along-to-antisemitic-song-survivors-in-court-x5l0k7m7d Blogger Alison Chabloz sings along to antisemitic song (((Survivors))) in court] (Times headline), [https://www.gettyimages.co.uk/detail/news-photo/blogger-alison-chabloz-who-is-accused-of-posting-anti-news-photo/903236526#/blogger-alison-chabloz-who-is-accused-of-posting-antisemitic-songs-on-picture-id903236526 Getty Images caption], and the body of all the mainstream sources?
# Should sources such as Jewish Times be included?
# Should Wikipedia suppress mention of this case as ''sub judice''?

'''Options'''

* I would say: '''yes it should be mentioned''', it is widely covered in the media and is a highly unusual private prosecution, possibly even the first of its kind - the issue of [[WP:BLPCRIME]] does not properly apply because the facts at issue are not in serious dispute. This is not a question of "did X do Y" but of "X admittedly did Y, was it a crime or not?"; '''yes we should use the word blogger''' but am not opposed to "and musician" if RS can be found (noting in passing that Google turns up pretty much nothing about her music other than this case); '''yes we should say antisemitic''' - the BBC is representative in saying ''accused of broadcasting "grossly offensive" anti-Semitic songs on the internet'', the two categories are not exclusive, but I have no problem including "grossly offensive and antisemitic" if that seems fairer; '''holocaust denier''' is the correct term per [[WP:WEASEL]] (and indeed revisionist is a redirect to denier); '''Yes we should name the target''' because all the mainstream sources do, sometimes in the headlines, and, more importantly, not only the pro-Jewish sites but also a large number of supportive non-RS sources also use her name, e..g. "[http://www.politicsforum.co.uk/forum/viewtopic.php?f=108&t=55964 The Persecution of Alison Chabloz]", "[http://boinnk.nl/143337/blood-libel-the-ritual-persecution-of-alison-chabloz/ Blood Libel: The Ritual Persecution of Alison Chabloz]" and so on - this also extends to several neo-Nazi sites, it's pretty clear that whatever the cause of her name being out there linked to this case, Wikipedia is not part of it, and indeed if we can't mention the name we arguably can't even cite some of the sourcees because it's in (e.g.) The Times article title; '''No''' we should not be including sources like the Jewish Times, they have an obvious bias and we have no need of them since we have much better sources for any content we might plausibly include; '''No''' Wikipedia can mention the case as long as we stick to what the mainstream media says, because the sources we quote have large legal departments and are quite well aware of what can be reported and what can't, we have no need to second-guess them. <b>[[User Talk:JzG|Guy]]</b> <small>([[User:JzG/help|Help!]])</small> 07:27, 18 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)#rfc_1DC8F0D|Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)]] expired 2018-05-22 11:01 ===

* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|842377066|PROP 842377066}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|842426473|PROP 842426473}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Should we delete talk pages that are currently blank and had never contained any actual discussions? [[WP:TPG]] says not to create empty talk pages just so that they can be used in the future. My G6 tagging of [[Talk:Host Healthcare]] has been declined by {{u|GorillaWarfare}}, so now we need an RfC. [[User:GeoffreyT2000|GeoffreyT2000]] ([[User talk:GeoffreyT2000|talk]]) 01:19, 22 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Riot shield#rfc_420A581|Talk:Riot shield]] expired 2018-05-22 23:01 ===
* Id: 420A581
* User: Zachary Klaas
* Date: 2018-05-12 20:26:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|840899531|POL 840899531}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|842512250|POL 842512250}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Following the advice given to me on the Dispute Resolution Page with respect to the immediately preceding section of this Talk page, I am now submitting a Request for Comments about whether this page on riot shields should clarify that, even if it is true that riot shields somehow encourage people at some psychological level to throw projectiles at the police, it is illegal in pretty much all jurisdictions to do so, and in many jurisdictions it is seriously illegal (that is, a felony).  I think the above exchange makes it clear what the matter of contention is, so I'm not going to rehash all that - but I do want to make clear that one editor offered the possibility of putting on the page something that does acknowledge this in presumably less tendentious language that people felt I was offering, and there is no reason that can't be done, whatever one thinks of my own approach to attempting those edits.  Don't snatch disagreement out of the jaws of agreement.  To my knowledge, no one is challenging the fact that jurisdictions generally do not allow the throwing of projectiles at the police, or indeed, at anyone else.  The debate was about whether it is necessary to say this here.  I don't understand why people are so dogmatically opposing one sentence that can clarify that Wikipedia is not treating illegal assaults on the police like they are not a big legal deal.  The best argument I have heard is that the sentence strikes people as unnecessary because it is presumed people already know that, but I suspect outside the small ecosystem of this page, there are people who might prefer the language were in there because people might indeed not know what it is assumed they know. [[User:Zachary Klaas|Zachary Klaas]] ([[User talk:Zachary Klaas|talk]]) 20:26, 12 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Portal guidelines#rfc_18D58A4|Wikipedia talk:Portal guidelines]] expired 2018-05-24 09:01 ===
* Id: 18D58A4
* Date: 2018-05-23 12:08:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|842597024|POLICY 842597024}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|842730030|POLICY 842730030}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
In light of new developments in the portal namespace, it is time for new and improved portal guidelines. These guidelines will help guide the updating and ongoing maintenance of the portal namespace.

The [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:Portal_guidelines&oldid=718250697 in-situ guidelines] were written in 2012, and have proven inadequate for guiding the creation and maintenance of portals. In addition, some parts of the guidelines were too restrictive and inhibited the evolution of portal design.  

As such we have removed mandatory design elements from the draft policy, and intend to add those (less imperatively) into [[Wikipedia:Portal/Instructions|the instructions]].

The new guidelines are intended to be sufficient to guard against unacceptable low quality portals, while not prejudicing against innovation (or already established markup). They will also guide editors into using the new transclusion templates to avoid content forks.

In short, this is a proposal to replace [[Wikipedia:Portal guidelines|this]] with the content of [[User:Cesdeva/sandbox11|this]] (minus the notices).
</br>
12:08, 23 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Music#rfc_9DEB168|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Music]] expired 2018-05-26 16:01 ===
* Id: 9DEB168
* Date: 2018-04-26 15:04:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|838381002|MEDIA 838381002}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|843061506|MEDIA 843061506}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This has been discussed before but consensus was not reached regarding whether there is, or should be, a notability criteria for record labels. [[WP:NCORP]] seems to be the guideline for record labels but there are editors who disagree, saying record labels should be based on [[WP:NMUSIC]] (#5). I am looking to gain consensus <s>to formally amend the relevant guidelines to accurately state what is needed and</s> to form a notability guideline for record labels. The previous discussion is archived [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Music/Archive 37#No criteria for labels|here]].

Should <s>the notability guideline for record labels be [[WP:NMUSIC]]</s> there be a notability guideline for record labels? <u style="text-decoration:none;font:1.1em/1em Arial Black;letter-spacing:-0.09em">[[User:KingAndGod|<u style="color:#3292a8">King</u>]]<u style="color:#6b32a8">And</u>[[User_talk:KingAndGod|<u style="color:#3292a8">God</u>]]</u> 15:04, 26 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Days of the year#rfc_E96F641|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Days of the year]] expired 2018-05-27 04:01 ===
* Id: E96F641
* User: Rochelimit
* Date: 2018-05-16 15:46:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|841569261|STYLE 841569261}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|841569264|POLICY 841569264}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|843137987|STYLE 843137987}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|843137988|POLICY 843137988}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Picture this, each DOY usually has about 200-300 lines. Imagine referencing every single line in a DOY, you will have a ref of another 200-300 lines, a mirror for each content. Each DOY will blow its size 2 times the original size.

I think it is extremely redundant and unnecessary. The original rule (before the changes on October 17, 2017) is that there is no need to place ref to every single line in DOY, as long as the ref is provided in the linked main article. It has always been like this for 10+ years. I respect the proposed intention, however, is this really achievable (given the extreme dynamics of the DOY articles)? is the pressure for compliance really worth it? would it help? 366 DOY each with 200-300 lines means 109,800 new refs should be added, which IMO is extremely redundant given each content actually already well-referenced in the linked main article in the first place (with multi-refs!). What will happen if the project stops in the middle just because we couldn't cope with the dynamic changes usually associated with DOY articles?

In my opinion, the task list of [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Days_of_the_year#Task_list Ensure each article has <nowiki>==References== </nowiki>{{tlx|reflist}} added] in the project page is very difficult to be implemented and would introduce major changes in the entire 366 DOY article as well as potential inconsistency throughout the 366 DOY articles for a long period of time. This is the first major change for 366 wiki articles after a decade.

To be honest, I proposed to have the rule of ''Ensure each article has References (reflist) added'' removed. I think it doesn't make sense and would cause quite a mess in the run. Now I just read it (I missed it!), I actually strongly oppose the proposal of [[Wikipedia_talk:WikiProject_Days_of_the_year#Exemption_from_WP:V|Exemption from WP:V]] discussed above. It would create a big burden to whoever responsible for completing this not enforceable project. As you may all know, each of the DOY articles is one of the most dynamic articles in Wikipedia, it is keep changed by random users on every single day. 

What are your opinions? Is this "project" of referencing really worth it? Let's open discussion for the sake of improvement?--[[User:Rochelimit|Rochelimit]] ([[User talk:Rochelimit|talk]]) 15:46, 16 May 2018 (UTC)}}
