=== [[Wikipedia talk:Miscellany for deletion#rfc_147B6D8|Wikipedia talk:Miscellany for deletion]] expired 2018-05-30 02:02 ===
* Id: 147B6D8
* User: Compassionate727
* Date: 2018-04-30 01:24:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|838910612|POLICY 838910612}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|843577175|POLICY 843577175}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Recent votes in various MfD discussions seem to indicate that there is a lack of consensus as to when it is appropriate to delete drafts and userpages. It seems to me that a large cause of the lack of consensus is ambiguity in the policies that address these issues, including [[WP:CSD]], [[WP:STALE]], and [[WP:UP]]. The lack of clarity is resulting in editors making wildly varied arguments, and while some of this is natural, the degree to which this is the case at MfD greatly exceeds that at AfD or RfD, for example. Furthermore, these variations seem to some degree to be the result of disagreements of philosophy, particularly about what the purpose the userspace serves, what purpose drafts serve, what purpose sandboxes serve, when deletion is appropriate, and numerous others. In order to shed light on this issue, I have compiled a list of questions which I hope will delve to the heart of this issue, that our discussion of them may shed light on these issues.

This is not a policy proposal, although discourse here may demonstrate the need for another RfC to propose policy. Rather, I wish to gather the opinions of various editors on the following questions. Some have more obvious answers than others, but I believe all to be worth asking and considering:

#What is (or should be) the difference between a [[Wikipedia:Draft space|draftspace]] draft and a [[Wikipedia:User pages|userspace]] draft?
##What is the benefit of distinguishing between the draftspace and the userspace for [[WP:CSD#G13|CSD G13]], and should CSD G13 be revised in any way to change its scope?
#What standards and/or uses make a userpage "useful to the Project" and, conversely, what failures make it "detrimental to the Project"?
##At what point does a useless draft become a violation of [[WP:CSD#U5|CSD U5]] and [[WP:NOTWEBHOST]]? For the purposes of CSD U5, what is a "plausible draft"?
##Can a stale userpage (one that has not been edited in more than a year) of an inactive user (someone who has not edited in more than a year) be considered "useful to the Project"?
##Does a userpage's uselessness alone warrant deletion at MfD or any other venue, or must it also pose some detriment to the Project, such as by qualifying for speedy deletion?
##If the answer to the above question is "depends", what other criteria should be considered in deciding about deletion?
#What distinguishes a sandbox from other userpages, and in what ways, if any, should policy treat them differently?
#Do drafts that serve no use to the Project and have no potential to be improved to the point of usefulness warrant deletion?
##Should the answer to the above question vary depending on whether said draft is in the userspace of the draftspace?
##What things give a draft potential for improvement or, conversely, deprive it of said potential? Is notability one of these things and, if so, how should we reconcile that with [[WP:NMFD]]?
#For the purposes of policy, what is the difference between blanking and soft deletion, and which is preferable in what situations? When are they preferable to normal deletion?
#Is it appropriate to move a stale userspace draft to draftspace if you have no intent of working on it?
#When, if ever, is it appropriate to ask an active editor to do something with a stale draft?

Discussion is not limited to these questions, and should include any and all pertinent topics. These are merely the questions that have been bouncing around in my head these past several days and as I was drafting this RfC.

Pinging to {{u|Legacypac}}, {{u|SmokeyJoe}}, {{u|Davey2010}}, {{u|Rhododendrites}}, {{u|Egaoblai}} and {{u|Robert McClenon}}, who have participated in multiple MfD discussions recently. <span style="white-space: nowrap;">—[[User:Compassionate727|Compassionate727]]&nbsp;<sup>([[User talk:Compassionate727|T]]·[[Special:Contributions/Compassionate727|C]])</sup></span> 01:24, 30 April 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Vitamin B3#rfc_366C98A|Talk:Vitamin B3]] expired 2018-06-03 03:29 ===
* Id: 366C98A
* User: Doc James
* Date: 2018-05-04 02:28:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|839540436|SCI 839540436}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|849116804|SCI 849116804}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
"'''Vitamin B<sub>3</sub>''', also known as '''vitamin B<sub>3</sub> complex''', is [[vitamin]] that includes three forms [[nicotinamide]] (niacinamide), [[niacin]] (nicotinic acid), and [[nicotinamide riboside]].<ref>{{cite book|last1=Krutmann|first1=Jean|last2=Humbert|first2=Philippe|title=Nutrition for Healthy Skin: Strategies for Clinical and Cosmetic Practice|date=2010|publisher=Springer Science & Business Media|isbn=9783642122644|page=153|url=https://books.google.ca/books?id=rUNZHmpBu2sC&pg=PA153|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|last1=Silvestre|first1=Ricardo|last2=Torrado|first2=Egídio|title=Metabolic Interaction in Infection|date=2018|publisher=Springer|isbn=9783319749327|page=364|url=https://books.google.ca/books?id=Y6VUDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA364|language=en}}</ref><ref name=Sti2013>{{cite book|last1=Stipanuk|first1=Martha H.|last2=Caudill|first2=Marie A.|title=Biochemical, Physiological, and Molecular Aspects of Human Nutrition - E-Book|date=2013|publisher=Elsevier Health Sciences|isbn=9780323266956|page=541|url=https://books.google.ca/books?id=XVNPAQAAQBAJ&pg=PA541|language=en}}</ref>"

*[https://books.google.ca/books?id=rUNZHmpBu2sC&pg=PA153 Ref 1] says "Niacin and nicotinamide, respectively, make up the vitamin B3 complex"
*[https://books.google.ca/books?id=Y6VUDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA364 Ref 2] says "Niacin or nicotinamate, together with its amide form nicotinamide, defines the group of vitamin B3 complex"
*[https://books.google.ca/books?id=XVNPAQAAQBAJ&pg=PA541 Ref 3] says "Three forms of vitamin B3" and shows Nicotinamide, Nicotinic acid, and nicotinamide riboside.

The last one was just found in 2004 which is why less sources mention it.

{{reflist-talk}}

Do the refs support this content? [[User:Doc James|<span style="color:#0000f1">'''Doc James'''</span>]] ([[User talk:Doc James|talk]] · [[Special:Contributions/Doc James|contribs]] · [[Special:EmailUser/Doc James|email]]) 02:28, 4 May 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
Should the map currently in the infobox be changed? Anatolia and its provinces have had many boundaries throughout a long history. The map currently in the lede one is non-specific as to the historical period it is referring to, with a very poorly worded caption. 

Based on the 1911 Britannica map below, it also seems the hand drawn boundary line of the current infobox map was not drawn accurately. I've checked the given citations and they fail verification. It is a bit hard to see, but Britannica has numbered the regions — the result is similar to the high-quality 2nd century AD map below.

I would like to replace this with a map that is attractive, accurate, with clear readable labels and a defined time period. I'm not set on any particular date or period.

=== [[Talk:Flag of Syria#rfc_6294308|Talk:Flag of Syria]] expired 2018-06-05 20:01 ===
* Id: 6294308
* User: 2003:CA:83C1:3500:DD19:E151:C1C3:7FC5
* Date: 2018-05-06 19:16:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|839952906|POL 839952906}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|844580279|POL 844580279}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I started a discussion already in the section immediately above, but starting a separate RFC section here in order to bring in more participation from a broader cross-section of Wikipedia community.

In brief, my proposal here has two components which, as noted above, would bring this article into line with the conventions already well established at other Syria-related articles, such as the main [[Syria]] article:

1. The Syrian government should be referred to as the "Syrian government" (or "government of Syria," or similar), not as the "Assad government," the "Assad regime," or anything along those lines.  Again, this is not only NPOV, but also would bring it in line with conventions elsewhere on Wikipedia.

2. The lede section should focus exclusively on the current primary flag of the government of Syria - i.e. the one with horizontal red, white, and black stripes and two green stars.

Naturally, historic flags of Syria should also be mentioned in the article, and the flags used by any group occupying parts of Syrian territory, whether a rebel group like the FSA, ISIS, or al-Nusra, or a foreign power like Israel or Turkey, could also be mentioned.  But the article should not suggest that any of these groups or their flags are somehow on equal footing with the actual government of Syria and its current flag.

As noted in the section above, the current status-quo for this article apparently emerged a number of years ago, towards the beginning of the war, when various rebel groups were rapidly advancing, and it looked like the government of Syria might fall at anytime and be replaced.  But this is no longer the case at all today. -[[Special:Contributions/2003:CA:83C1:3500:DD19:E151:C1C3:7FC5|2003:CA:83C1:3500:DD19:E151:C1C3:7FC5]] ([[User talk:2003:CA:83C1:3500:DD19:E151:C1C3:7FC5|talk]]) 19:16, 6 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:List of modern names for biblical place names#rfc_8F796DF|Talk:List of modern names for biblical place names]] expired 2018-06-06 00:01 ===
* Id: 8F796DF
* User: Davidbena
* Date: 2018-05-06 23:08:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|839983101|HIST 839983101}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|839983107|POL 839983107}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|844611629|HIST 844611629}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|844611635|POL 844611635}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
In the current article which treats on the modern names for biblical sites, there is an entry for the "Country Name." As is known, many of these biblical sites are in Israel, also known as Palestine, being the same geographical country. However, there has been an attempt to politicize the "Country Name," by writing either "Palestinian territories" or "Israel," as if it were two separate countries. It is my view that we ought to be apolitical about the "Country Name," and that wherever these two designations apply in this particular article, we should write both "Palestine/Israel." In this way we keep this issue neutral, in accordance with Wikipedia's policy in [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Requests_for_arbitration/Palestine-Israel_articles Palestine-Israel articles]. Any other views on how we should proceed here? Please add your comment.[[User:Davidbena|Davidbena]] ([[User talk:Davidbena|talk]]) 23:08, 6 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Hospitals#rfc_90D995C|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Hospitals]] expired 2018-06-06 16:01 ===
* Id: 90D995C
* User: ClevelandClinicES
* Date: 2018-05-07 15:06:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Economy,_trade,_and_companies|prev|840078980|ECON 840078980}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|840078981|SCI 840078981}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Economy,_trade,_and_companies|prev|844706221|ECON 844706221}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|844706226|SCI 844706226}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I'm seeking further comment to see if it is possible to make the rules clearer for how hospital reputation, rankings, ratings, and awards are handled on Wikipedia. What should the established standard be for how ratings and rankings are included on hospital Wikipedia articles?

A bit more background, in case it's helpful: As I have proposed updates to [[Cleveland Clinic]]'s existing ''Reputation'' section, a common response from volunteer editors is that other hospital articles should not be used for guidance. I looked at the Wikipedia articles for the nine hospitals in ''U.S. News & World Report''{{'}}s Top 10. Of those, six of the articles either listed the hospitals' specialty rankings or contained a table: [[Mayo Clinic]], [[Johns Hopkins Hospital]], [[UCSF Medical Center]], [[Michigan Medicine]], [[New York-Presbyterian Hospital]], and [[Stanford Health Care]]. Three did not: [[Massachusetts General Hospital]], [[Ronald Reagan UCLA Medical Center]], and [[Hospital of the University of Pennsylvania]]. There are other differences in how this info is handled: While the Cleveland Clinic article has a ''Reputation'' section, Mayo Clinic, Johns Hopkins Hospital, and Michigan Medicine have ''Rankings'', New York-Presbyterian Hospital has ''Awards and recognition'', UCSF Medical Center and Stanford Health Care have rankings listed in the introduction.

I hope this conversation leads to more discussion on ways to create a set of standards for streamlined further development of all hospital articles on Wikipedia. Thanks, [[User:ClevelandClinicES|ClevelandClinicES]] ([[User talk:ClevelandClinicES|talk]]) 15:06, 7 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Bust of Cristiano Ronaldo#rfc_EA39FDC|Talk:Bust of Cristiano Ronaldo]] expired 2018-06-08 20:01 ===
* Id: EA39FDC
* User: Another Believer
* Date: 2018-05-09 19:22:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|840423080|MEDIA 840423080}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|840423081|SOC 840423081}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|845023573|MEDIA 845023573}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|845023578|SOC 845023578}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
'''Request for comment: Should [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo&oldid=840385297 this version of the "Bust of Cristiano Ronaldo"] exist in the main space?'''

Back in April 2017, the [[Bust of Cristiano Ronaldo]] article was redirected to the [[Cristiano Ronaldo International Airport]] article, per [[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Bust of Cristiano Ronaldo|this AfD discussion]]. In March 2018, I revisited [[Draft:Bust of Cristiano Ronaldo]] (now merged as the result of [[Wikipedia_talk:WikiProject_Public_Art/Archive_2#Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo_2|this discussion]] and [[User_talk:KJP1#Bust|this discussion]]), after a ''second'' bust depicting Ronaldo was created by the same artist. Again, the project received significant secondary coverage in reliable sources.

I started [[Talk:Cristiano_Ronaldo_International_Airport#Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo,_part_2|this discussion on the airport article's talk page]], and invited editors who participated in previous discussions to weigh in, including editors who commented in the AfD discussion. I made the mistake of also discussing the same topic in other locations, including [[Talk:Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo#Merge]] and [[Wikipedia:Deletion review/Log/2018 May 9]], and at several WikiProjects in an attempt to get more editors to weigh on in the discussion. I take responsibility for starting discussions in too many spaces, but I was just trying to get wider community input.

My attempt to ask for help [[User_talk:Number_57#Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo|here]] was not particularly helpful, and when I [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo&type=revision&diff=840386438&oldid=840385297 tried to make updates to the redirected article] (with "under construction" template displayed), {{u|Number 57}} reverted. I've since been [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Talk:Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo&diff=840396452&oldid=840396205 accused of trying to hide discussions] and [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo&diff=prev&oldid=840387166 threatened with WP:ANI]. I was just trying to make additional expansions and collapse/archive some of the side discussions and centralize comments [[Talk:Cristiano_Ronaldo_International_Airport#Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo,_part_2|here]]. I'm not looking to ''hide'' dissenting opinions.

Now, I've noticed editors with an interest in sports seem not to like this article, while editors with an interest in public art/sculpture do. I know some editors will be upset that I've opened this request for comment, and I expect we will see similar voting based on ''sports vs. work of art''. This is why I feel a new discussion needs to be had by a wider net of Wikipedia editors, and on this article talk page, not the airport article's talk page. Many editors have contributed to this discussion, but few have commented on the ''most recent version of the article'', which has recently-merged content from the draft space, and can be seen '''[https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bust_of_Cristiano_Ronaldo&oldid=840386438 here]'''.

I am looking for editors to '''re-assess the notability of this topic'''. The article now has information about ''two original works of art'', both of which have received significant press coverage. I've used the "Media, the arts, and architecture" and
"Society, sports, and culture" parameters for this RfC.

Thank you. ---[[User:Another Believer|<span style="color:navy">Another Believer</span>]] <sub>([[User talk:Another Believer|<span style="color:#C60">Talk</span>]])</sub> 19:22, 9 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)#rfc_2EE6635|Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)]] expired 2018-06-10 19:01 ===
* Id: 2EE6635
* User: TonyBallioni
* Date: 2018-05-11 18:39:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|840724553|POLICY 840724553}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|845282671|POLICY 845282671}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The deletion of drafts via MfD was previously discussed over two years ago in  [[Wikipedia_talk:Notability/Archive_58#RfC:_Does_WP:N_apply_to_drafts_in_userspace_or_draftspace.3F|this RfC]] that concluded that drafts should not be subject to the notability criteria, but that there may be other valid reasons for the deletions of drafts. Reading the comments of the RfC and the close, there also seemed to be agreement that drafts should be works in progress, eventually expected to meet mainspace standards. Currently, it is possible to continually resubmit a declined draft to AfC with no changes while not meeting any of the CSD criteria or failing [[WP:NOTWEBHOST]] and effectively stay in draft space forever. This has caused some back and forth at MfD as what to do with these articles. To help provide clarity for this situation, I am proposing [[WP:NMFD]] be modified to read the following (updated text in red):
{{talkquote|Drafts are not subject to [[WP:ACSD|article deletion]] criteria like "no context" or no indication of notability so creators may have time to establish notability. Drafts may be nominated for deletion at [[Wikipedia:Miscellany for deletion]], but not {{red|solely based upon a}} concern about notability. {{red|A draft that has been repeatedly resubmitted and declined at AfC without any substantial improvement may be deleted at [[Wikipedia:Miscellany for deletion]] if consensus determines that it is unlikely to ever meet the requirements for mainspace and it otherwise meets one of the [[Wikipedia:Deletion_policy#Reasons_for_deletion|reasons for deletion]] outlined in [[Wikipedia:Deletion policy]].}}}}
[[User:TonyBallioni|TonyBallioni]] ([[User talk:TonyBallioni|talk]]) 18:39, 11 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)#rfc_35DC7FF|Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)]] expired 2018-06-10 19:01 ===
* Id: 35DC7FF
* User: Rod57
* Date: 2018-05-29 16:02:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|843514724|TECH 843514724}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|843514727|PROP 843514727}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|847401665|TECH 847401665}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|847401667|PROP 847401667}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
A [[Wikipedia:Village_pump_(proposals)/Archive_145#Disable_messages_left_by_InternetArchiveBot|previous RfC]] halted new talk page posts by InternetArchiveBot. 

This RfC is to see if there is consensus to delete the posts. It affects about 1 million talk pages. An [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Talk:Namibian_Port_Authority&oldid=825153665 example post] that would be deleted.

There are two options for deletion:
:'''#1''' - a bot edits the 1 million pages deleting posts. Archived talk pages will be left alone. Bot operator [[User:GreenC]] has volunteered.
:'''#2''' - the wording of the post is modified to give users permission to delete posts if they want to. Since talk page posts normally can't be deleted by other users, it would remove that restriction. The wording can easily be changed via the {{tlx|sourcecheck}} template, '''it would not require every page be edited'''.

Please !vote '''support''' or '''oppose'''. Clarify choice of method #1 and/or #2 in order of preference. 

- [[User:Rod57|Rod57]] ([[User talk:Rod57|talk]]) 16:02, 29 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Military history#rfc_7E3F270|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Military history]] expired 2018-06-11 08:01 ===
* Id: 7E3F270
* User: Mztourist
* Date: 2018-06-07 10:42:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|845009250|HIST 845009250}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|845358920|HIST 845358920}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I have unfortunately been engaged in edit wars on the Infoboxes of various Vietnam War battle pages with a User who is adding "US claims" or "US reports" or the wikilink to [[Body count#Vietnam War]] before the figures for North Vietnamese/Vietcong casualties. I am fine with any one of US report/claim/source/body count being added, showing that this is the US account of North Vietnamese/Vietcong casualties and I believe that this is in line with other battle pages, particularly those where casualties are contested. However this User has in various case inserted the formulation "US Claims: X killed ([[Body count#Vietnam war|body count]])" or even "US Source: X killed ([[Body count#Vietnam war|body count]] claim)" which to me is like saying "US claim claim claim" and I believe that is POV designed to (further) undermine the credibility of US claims of North Vietnamese/Vietcong losses which are already discussed in detail at [[Body count]]. Can you please advise below if you support or oppose the use of only one of report, claim, source or [[Body count#Vietnam war|body count]] on all Vietnam War battle pages. regards [[User:Mztourist|Mztourist]] ([[User talk:Mztourist|talk]]) 10:42, 7 June 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
Above on the article's talk page, there is a dispute with regard to critical reception material in the article (the [[Rey (Star Wars)#Parentage|Parentage section]]). One argument is that [[Kylo Ren]] didn't state the actual words "they are nobodies" to [[Rey (Star Wars)|Rey]] about her parents. Therefore, we shouldn't state that Kylo Ren said this. In contrast to this view, reliable sources (seen below in the Discussion section) state that Kylo Ren told or led Rey to believe that her parents are nobodies, despite not using the actual word "nobodies." Therefore, the other argument is that we should be able to report that Kylo Ren did this. So can/should we?

In 2011, the page ''WP:Think of Wikipe-tan!'' was deleted after a consensus that concerns that the page could "drive female editors away" represented a "real and theoretical potential to harm the project".<ref>[[Wikipedia:Miscellany for deletion/Wikipedia:Think of Wikipe-tan!]]</ref>

* Id: 28455FC
* User: Floydian
* Date: 2018-05-14 18:00:00

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|841230599|HIST 841230599}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|841537549|SCI 841537549}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|845723413|HIST 845723413}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|845723416|SCI 845723416}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I've placed this under geography, although it could go under biology as well. There appears to be a long-waged edit war on this page with regards to the coordinates for Hyperion. I've located a past discussion regarding the need to cite coordinates, as anybody can verify them by going to the location. IMO, this is equivalent to a photograph claiming to be of a certain location.

Other arguments raised in this particular topic are that the park services or discoverer don't want want the location made publicly available due to fears of vandalism (which is not backed by a source).

Should coordinates be included? Do they, and by extension all of the million or so coordinates on en.wiki, require citation? Do the opinions of the park services hold any weight? Most importantly, why do you take that stance? - '''[[User:Floydian|<span style="color: #5A5AC5;">Floydian</span>]]'''&nbsp;<sup>[[User_talk:Floydian|<span style="color: #3AAA3A;">τ</span>]]</sup> <sub>[[Special:Contributions/Floydian|<span style="color: #3AAA3A;">¢</span>]]</sub> 18:00, 14 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Bipartisan Report#rfc_F57710B|Talk:Bipartisan Report]] expired 2018-06-15 06:01 ===
* Id: F57710B
* User: PCHS-NJROTC
* Date: 2018-05-25 16:04:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|842928659|MEDIA 842928659}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|842928662|POL 842928662}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|845943848|MEDIA 845943848}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|845943849|POL 845943849}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I am the creator of this article, and the neutrality of the article was immediately questioned upon the article's creation. At the time of the article's creation, almost all mentions of the site in [[WP:RS|reliable sources]] were negative, and nothing has changed since then. The site's articles have been attack by both [http://www.politifact.com/personalities/bipartisan-report/ Politifact] and [https://www.snopes.com/tag/bipartisan-report/ Snopes], which is worth mentioning in the article since both are reliable sources. However, there have been repeated attempts by IP addresses belonging to travel-related networks ([[Gogo Inflight Internet]], a hotel, etc) trying to whitewash the article of any mentions of criticism (see [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:Contributions/12.130.117.181 this], [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:Contributions/12.130.117.152 this], [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:Contributions/49.231.236.17 this], and [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Talk:Bipartisan_Report&diff=next&oldid=824965845 this]). Most recently, [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:Contributions/Kk01011991 a relatively new user removed all references to criticism of the website]. I suspect someone who does a lot of traveling is responsible for all of these edits, either deliberately using IPs around the world for the purposes of [[WP:Sockpuppetry|deception]] or just out of convenience. 

I propose that the analysis of Bipartisan Report's claims by [[Snopes]] and [[Politifact]] be readded to the article, with as neutral tone as possible. A previous RfC stated there was consensus to readd the material, but in light of the objections (possibly from sockpuppets), I've decided it is best to do another RfC since U.S. politics is a controversial subject. [[User:PCHS-NJROTC|<span style="color: red; font-family: Comic Sans MS;">PCHS-NJROTC</span>]] <sup>[[User talk:PCHS-NJROTC|<span style="color: black; font-family: Comic Sans MS;">(Messages)Have a blessed day.</span>]]</sup> 16:04, 25 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Campaign Against Antisemitism#rfc_6836150|Talk:Campaign Against Antisemitism]] expired 2018-06-17 08:01 ===
* Id: 6836150
* Date: 2018-05-18 07:27:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Religion_and_philosophy|prev|841883307|RELI 841883307}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|841883313|SOC 841883313}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Religion_and_philosophy|prev|846225741|RELI 846225741}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|846225743|SOC 846225743}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
CAA brought a highly unusual private prosecution against Alison Chabloz. Ms Chabloz disputes the inclusion and characterisation of this content, specifically: she disputes that she is accused of antisemitic acts but instead the charges relate to "grossly offensive" words, stating that "{{tq|Wikipedia is supposedly independent of mainstream media. What's the point of an independent outlet that simply parrots mainstream soundbites?
}}" and denigrating the coverage as {{tq|moronic mainstream media articles}}; she asserts that she should be described as a musician not a blogger, and that the term blogger is a deliberate insult; she insists that she should be called a "holocaust revisionist" not a "holocaust denier". The following questions appear to be germane:
# Should the private prosecution be included?
# Should the target of the prosecution be described as a "blogger" per [http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-derbyshire-43321482 Blogger claims "no proof" gas chambers killed Jewish people] (BBC), [https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/blogger-alison-chabloz-sings-along-to-antisemitic-song-survivors-in-court-x5l0k7m7d Blogger Alison Chabloz sings along to antisemitic song (((Survivors))) in court] (The Times), [http://www.itv.com/news/2018-01-11/blogger-mocked-anne-frank-and-holocaust-survivors-court-told/ Blogger 'mocked Anne Frank and Holocaust survivors', court told] (ITV)?
# Should the target of the prosecution be characterised as antisemitic, per [http://courtnewsuk.co.uk/judge-considering-verdict-on-antisemitic-songwriter/ Court News] and the other RS listed above?
# Should the target of the prosecution be characterised as a [[holocaust revisionist]], [http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-derbyshire-42637888 'Holocaust revisionist'] in scare quotes as per the BBC, or a [[holocaust denier]]?
# Should the target of the prosecution be named, as per [https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/blogger-alison-chabloz-sings-along-to-antisemitic-song-survivors-in-court-x5l0k7m7d Blogger Alison Chabloz sings along to antisemitic song (((Survivors))) in court] (Times headline), [https://www.gettyimages.co.uk/detail/news-photo/blogger-alison-chabloz-who-is-accused-of-posting-anti-news-photo/903236526#/blogger-alison-chabloz-who-is-accused-of-posting-antisemitic-songs-on-picture-id903236526 Getty Images caption], and the body of all the mainstream sources?
# Should sources such as Jewish Times be included?
# Should Wikipedia suppress mention of this case as ''sub judice''?
<b>[[User Talk:JzG|Guy]]</b> <small>([[User:JzG/help|Help!]])</small> 07:27, 18 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Trans man#rfc_BC48119|Talk:Trans man]] expired 2018-06-19 14:01 ===
* Id: BC48119
* User: Userwoman
* Date: 2018-05-20 13:14:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|842139279|SOC 842139279}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|846557577|SOC 846557577}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Disagreement over how to define trans man. One side states that any person who is born male is a man (male human) and the other side states that any person who identifies as a man is a man (masculine identity). Both sides argue that their position is supported by alternate interpretations of the same sources.

*[https://www.cdc.gov/hiv/group/gender/transgender/index.html CDC] "People who were assigned the female sex at birth but identify as men"
*[https://www.apa.org/topics/lgbt/transgender.pdf APA] "People who were assigned female but identify and live as male"
*[https://hr.cornell.edu/sites/default/files/trans%20terms.pdf Cornell] "Individuals assigned female at birth who identify as male"

This major edit was made on the trans woman page without any preceding discussion and was later adopted by the trans man page. 08:43, 19 October 2016‎ Picture of a Sunny Day (inactive) (First sentence was unnecessarily verbose. Trans women are women according to MOS: IDENTITY). Previous definition: A trans woman is a transgender person who was assigned male at birth but whose gender identity is that of a woman. Current definition: A trans woman is a woman who was assigned male at birth.

Was this change justified? If not, what is the best definition of trans man and trans woman? [[User:Userwoman|Userwoman]] ([[User talk:Userwoman|talk]]) 13:14, 20 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Songs#rfc_EDC719B|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Songs]] expired 2018-06-20 15:01 ===
* Id: EDC719B
* User: Another Believer
* Date: 2018-05-21 14:27:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|842297146|MEDIA 842297146}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|846729828|MEDIA 846729828}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Too often, "songs by artist" categories associate an artist's entire repertoire with one or more genres, even when song articles include no mention of those genres.

For example: [[:Category:Lady Gaga songs]] is a subcategory of "American synthpop songs", "Dance-pop songs", and "Electropop songs", yet entries include "[[Cheek to Cheek]]" and "[[Nature Boy]]", which are ''definitely'' none of the aforementioned genres.

Should we stop classifying "songs by artist" categories by genre? There is an ongoing discussion at [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Songs]], but I'm submitting a request for comment to generate more discussion. Thank you. --[[User:Another Believer|<span style="color:navy">Another Believer</span>]] <sub>([[User talk:Another Believer|<span style="color:#C60">Talk</span>]])</sub> 14:27, 21 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Alaska#rfc_2C9F32D|Talk:Alaska]] expired 2018-06-22 21:01 ===
* Id: 2C9F32D
* User: Beeblebrox
* Date: 2018-05-23 20:11:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|842661161|HIST 842661161}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|847087685|HIST 847087685}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
You know what I’m talking about. That map. The map of the states they had in the classroom when you were a kid, the one that show Alaska in a box where Baja California should be. 
[[File:Map of USA AK.svg|thumb|Shows where Alaska is not, and the scale is grossly incorrect.]]
[[File:Alaska in United States (US50).svg|thumb|Shows where Alaska actually is, and with a much improved sense of scale.]]
So, if the purpose of Wikipedia is to spread knowledge, should we not use the map that actually shows reality? We already do in this article, because I changed it some time ago, but should we not use this, if not universally, at least in all articles that are actually ''about Alaska''? Because as of right now there are over a hundred articles using the highly inaccurate map and only 5 using the more accurate one. If this request succeeds in forming a consensus for change I intend to file a request for a bot to make the necessary changes, or failing that I’ll do it myself. [[User:Beeblebrox|Beeblebrox]] ([[User talk:Beeblebrox|talk]]) 20:11, 23 May 2018 (UTC)}}

Recently an editor added 4 external links to a certain website, First of all I think that is overkill. Apart from that, I think that none of the links is especially valuable, and see no compelling reason they should be included. In addition, the source in question, the [[Applied Research Institute–Jerusalem]], has a very clear political agenda, and I am always wary of science which is being used for the attainment of political goals. All in all I would like to see opinions of editors regarding the desirableness of these links. I would also propose that in the case that a <u>clear</u> consensus should emerge among editors <u>who have no prior involvement</u> in this article, and on that condition only, this discussion could be used for similar issues on related articles. === [[Talk:Ideological bias on Wikipedia#rfc_07279DA|Talk:Ideological bias on Wikipedia]] expired 2018-06-24 22:01 ===
* Id: 07279DA
* User: Netoholic
* Date: 2018-06-16 06:11:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Economy,_trade,_and_companies|prev|846230629|ECON 846230629}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|846230631|HIST 846230631}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|846230632|POL 846230632}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Economy,_trade,_and_companies|prev|850496186|ECON 850496186}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|850496189|HIST 850496189}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|850496191|POL 850496191}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
{{quote|In 2013, the [[Croatian Wikipedia#2013 controversy about right-wing bias|Croatian-language version of Wikipedia]] gained media attention after the daily newspaper ''[[Jutarnji list]]'' reported on critic's concerns that administrators and editors on the website were projecting a [[Far-right politics in Croatia|right-wing]] bias into topics such as the [[Ustashe]] regime, [[anti-fascism]], [[Serbs of Croatia|Serbs]], the [[LGBT]] community, and [[gay marriage]]. Many of the critics were former editors of the website who said they had been exiled for expressing concern. The small size of the Croatian Wikipedia — as of September 2013, it had 466 active editors of which 27 were administrators — was cited as a major factor. Two days after the story broke, [[Ministry of Science and Education (Croatia)|Croatian Minister]] [[Željko Jovanović]] advised students not to use the website.<ref name="dailydot">{{cite web |url=https://www.dailydot.com/layer8/croatian-wikipedia-fascist-takeover-controversy-right-wing/ |title=How pro-fascist ideologues are rewriting Croatia's history|last=Sampson|first=Tim|work=[[The Daily Dot]]|accessdate=May 25, 2018|date=October 1, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|last1=Penić|first1=Goran|url=http://www.jutarnji.hr/radikalni-desnicari-preuzeli-uredivanje-hr-wikipedije--ndh-nije-svjesno-bila-totalitarna--a-antifasizam-se-bori-protiv-svih-sloboda-/1125398/|title=Desničari preuzeli uređivanje hrvatske Wikipedije|work=[[Jutarnji list]]|date=10 September 2013|language=Croatian|trans-title=Right-wing editors took over the Croatian Wikipedia|accessdate=May 25, 2018}}</ref><ref name="inserbia">{{cite news|url=https://inserbia.info/today/2013/09/fascist-movement-takes-over-croatian-wikipedia/|title=Fascist movement takes over Croatian Wikipedia?|publisher=InSerbia Today|date=September 11, 2013|accessdate=May 25, 2018}}</ref><ref name="GayStarNews">{{cite news|author1=reporter3|title=Trolls hijack Wikipedia to turn articles against gays|url=https://www.gaystarnews.com/article/trolls-hijack-wikipedia-turn-articles-against-gays170913/#gs.1evuSEQ|accessdate=26 May 2018|work=[[Gay Star News]]|date=September 17, 2013}}</ref> In 2018, historian Hrvoje Klasic of the [[Faculty of Humanities and Social Sciences, University of Zagreb]] told the [[Balkan Investigative Reporting Network]] (BIRN) that he often refers students to the [[English Wikipedia]] instead of their native Croatian, especially for topics on [[History of Croatia|Croation history]]. Goran Hutinec, also a historian at Faculty of Humanities and Social Sciences, said of the Croatian Wikipedia that is has "many shortcomings, factual mistakes and ideologically loaded language".<ref name="BIRN">{{cite news|last1=Milekic|first1=Sven|title=How Croatian Wikipedia Made a Concentration Camp Disappear|url=http://www.balkaninsight.com/en/article/how-croatian-wikipedia-made-a-concentration-camp-disappear-03-23-2018|accessdate=26 May 2018|work=[[Balkan Insight]]|publisher=Balkan Investigative Reporting Network|date=March 26, 2018|location=Zagreb}}</ref>}}

{{reflist-talk}}

Should the above event related to the Croatian Wikipedia be included in this article? --[[User:Netoholic|Netoholic]] [[User talk:Netoholic|@]]  06:11, 16 June 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
I edited this page (as I did in 2016, when I was [[User:FiscalSpace|FiscalSpace]]: took a long wikibreak and couldn't remember my password when I rejoined, so took on a similar name, which seemed the right thing to do). I then recently returned to this page and noted the allegations of sockpuppetry and carried out a revision that took it back to the pre-sockpuppet version. I don't think anything I did was vandalism in any way. However, now a user ([[User:Mcmanusbr|McManusbr]]) has reverted my edits and (a) accuses me of "vandal like edits" and (b) says I have a "longstanding grudge" against the doctor. 

Two things: first, I don't think any of my edits were vandalism, but I would welcome the views of more experienced editors; second, how could the user know - or suspect - that I have a 'personal grudge' against Dr Treacy without being either Dr Treacy or someone very close to him - in which case the page is being edited by the subject of the page or someone close to him, which gives rise to a  conflict of interest and is also entirely consistent with the history of previous Dr Treacy pages -see below? I don't, by the way, have a grudge against him, just against the advertising that this page seems to indulge in.

I know that previous checkuser has exposed sockpuppets continually editing this page (which is why I reverted back to a reasonably pre-sockpuppet version): I wonder about [[User:Mcmanusbr|McManusbr]], too.

In any event, I think that someone more experienced that I should make a call on this page. I'm not going to get into a fight with a user who throws around accusations of vandalism, but the history of this particular page and the previous history of other pages set out below, should give pause for thought before calling my edits vandalism and favouring the most recent version. Particular problems with this page are (a) that almost every fact recorded on it is traceable back only to the subject of the article himself and claims he has made (something  which my edits looked to reflect) and (b) that this page seems to have been edited only by sock-puppets and people close to the subject. 

Having said all that though, insofar as certain awards are now referenced in the most recent version, that seems to be an improvement.

Looking back at my 2016 comments I noted that someone called [[User:Peege1969|Peege1969]] (more or less the same twitter handle as subject) added the photo. Since then the same user reverted a previous edit that someone with an interest in the subject of the article might have wanted to see reverted. Anyway, it's all - as Douglas Adams said - an SEP.

{{rfcquote|text=
*Shall the article '''[[Living dinosaur]]''' be changed from a standard format article, to a disambiguation list-format article?

'''Note''' - The article has existed since 2006, starting out as more of a list-type page, but evolving into an article with prose by 2010. There were [[Talk:Living_dinosaur#Cryptozoology_section|recent discussions]] about expansion by adding sentences on the [[Tuatara]] and [[Enigma moth]], creatures actually called ''living dinosaurs'' in sources. Other article contents have also been [[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Partridge Creek monster (Cryptid)|discussed about merging]] into the ''Living dinosaur'' article. However, a couple editors have expressed a desire to change ''Living dinosaur'' into a [[Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Disambiguation pages|non-article formal disambiguation list-form page]] with little to no prose, [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Living_dinosaur&oldid=843369017 such as with this example].

I thought it best that more editors should have eyes and comments on what final form a 12 year-old article should take to best serve our readers. Major editors of this article and the proper WikiProjects should be informed. I felt a 12 year-old article warranted more discussion than just three or four editors when such a huge change could be taking place. Thanks. [[User:Fyunck(click)|Fyunck(click)]] ([[User talk:Fyunck(click)|talk]]) 21:41, 29 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_93D5250|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2018-06-29 18:01 ===
* Id: 93D5250
* User: Beyond My Ken#top
* Date: 2018-06-29 06:11:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|848010804|POL 848010804}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|848010807|POLICY 848010807}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|848085509|POL 848085509}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|848085511|POLICY 848085511}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Should any editor who changes "far-right" to "far-left" in describing Nazism, Fascism, neo-Nazism, and other close-related ideologies be subject to immediate blocking as a disruptive editor, tantamount to a vandal?

'''Survey (no threaded discussion, please)'''

*'''Yes''' -  This is a constant problem in protecting articles on these subjects from damage, and a tool is needed to nip the damage these editors do in the bud.{{parabr}}In the real world of academics, historians and other experts, there is absolutely no doubt that Nazism, Fascism, neo-Nazism and other closely-related ideologies exist on the far-right of the right/left political spectrum, despite the fact that some instantiations of these ideologies espouse or put into effect some views which are usually associated with socialism, a leftist ideology.  Given that the placement of the political systems described is firmly fixed by expert consensus as being on the far-right, and that this is unlikely to change any time in the near future, any editor who makes changes of "far-right" to "far-left" is clearly someone editing in accord with their [[WP:FRINGE]] personal point of view, and are therefore violating [[WP:NPOV]], as well as engaging in [[WP:OR|original research]].  Since no reputable expert agrees with their edits, they are also making edits which are unverifiable on their face, violating [[WP:V]]. The majority of editors who engage in this activity do so without providing any sources, and those that do are violating [[WP:RS]].{{parabr}}Such editors should be considered as being [[WP:Disruptive editing|disruptive]], and as ''de facto'' vandals, and when their edits are presented to an administrator, the editor in question should be immediately blocked unless there is overwhelming credible evidence to provide a basis on which the admin can invoke administrative discretion and not make the block.  The '''''presumption''''', however, should be that editors making such changes are to be blocked, and an admin who does not do so should be prepared to explain their decision to the community on demand, per [[WP:ADMINACCT]]. <small class="autosigned">—&nbsp;Preceding [[Wikipedia:Signatures|unsigned]] comment added by [[User:Beyond My Ken|Beyond My Ken]] ([[User talk:Beyond My Ken#top|talk]] • [[Special:Contributions/Beyond My Ken|contribs]]) 06:11, 29 June 2018 (UTC)}}

* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Should the article mention Melania Trump's "I don't really care" jacket?

Something like:

{{tq2|In June 2018, following immense public opposition to the [[Trump administration family separation policy]] , Melania Trump traveled to visit a children's shelter in Texas. At the outset of the trip, she appeared wearing a $39 [[Zara (retailer)|Zara]] military-style jacket emblazoned with the phrase "I REALLY DON’T CARE, DO U?". The controversial jacket drew worldwide reactions, some describing the fashion choice as "Insensitive", "heartless" and "unthinking". Her staff dismissed concerns that the jacket conveyed a hidden message.<ref name=Friedman>{{cite web | url=https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/21/style/zara-jacket-melania-trump.html | title=Melania Trump, Agent of Coat Chaos | work=[[The New York Times]] | date=June 21, 2018 | accessdate=June 25, 2018 | last=Friedman | first=Vanessa}}</ref><ref name=Birnbaum>{{cite web | url=http://thehill.com/homenews/administration/393780-former-first-ladys-chief-of-staff-melania-trumps-staff-knew-the | title=Former first lady’s chief of staff: Melania Trump’s staff knew the jacket would ‘send a message’ | work=[[The Hill (newspaper)|]] | date=June 23, 2018 | accessdate=June 25, 2018 | last=Birnbaum | first=Emily}}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.bbc.com/news/entertainment-arts-44600087 | title=Stars respond to Melania's 'I don't really care" jacket | work=[[BBC]] | date=June 25, 2018 | accessdate=June 25, 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url=https://indianexpress.com/article/lifestyle/fashion/melania-trump-jacket-controversy-i-really-dont-care-do-u-jacket-faces-plagiarism-charges-r13-brand-5232780/ | title=Melania Trump’s infamous ‘I really don’t care, do u?’ Zara jacket faces plagiarism charges | work=[[The Indian Express]] | date=June 25, 2018 | accessdate=June 25, 2018}}</ref>}}  
{{Sources-talk}}

=== [[Talk:Mass killings under Communist regimes#rfc_03AC701|Talk:Mass killings under Communist regimes]] expired 2018-06-30 01:01 ===
* Id: 03AC701
* User: Paul Siebert
* Date: 2018-06-05 05:41:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|844480757|HIST 844480757}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|848912037|HIST 848912037}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I am asking about the most neutral way to present the figures of "Communist death toll" presented by Courtois in the introduction to [[the Black Book of Communism]] (aka BB).

*In the introduction to the Black Book of Communism, the editor of this volume, Coirtois, provides the figures of communist death toll. These figures, as well as the very idea to combine loosely connected events under a single category, has been severely criticized. The examples of criticism are provided [[talk:Mass killings under Communist regimes#BB reviews|here]], and many critics blame Courtois in manipulation with figures and their deliberate inflation. In addition, the idea to connect the deaths with some "generic Communism" concept (defined down to the common denominator of party movements founded by intellectuals) has been criticised by other authors,<ref>Michael David-Fox, On the Primacy of Ideology: Soviet Revisionists and Holocaust Deniers (In Response to Martin Malia). ''Kritika: Explorations in Russian and Eurasian History'', Volume 5, Number 1, Winter 2004 (New Series), pp. 81-105 (Article) DOI: [https://doi.org/10.1353/kri.2004.0007]</ref> who argues that a connection between, e.g., events in Pol Pot's Cambodia and Stalin's USSR is far from evident, and Pol Pot’s study of Marxism in Paris is insufficient for connecting radical Soviet industrialism and the Khmer Rouge’s murderous anti-urbanism under the same category. Furthermore, the figures produced by Courtois are always presented to advocate the idea that Communism was greater evil than Nazism. This idea has been criticized by many authors<ref>Jens Mecklenburg and Wolfgang Wippermann, eds, ‘Roter Holocaust’? Kritik des Schwarzbuchs des Kommunismus [A ‘Red Holocaust’? A Critique of the Black Book of Communism], Hamburg, Konkret Verlag Literatur, 1998; ISBN 3–89458–169–7</ref>

Many critics also note that the Courtois's introduction to the BB is the most problematic part of this collective volume, and most criticism is focused on it. Even some contributors to the BB publicly disassociated themselves from the conclusions presented in the introduction (see the link to the talk page), and from the figures in particular.
In connection to that, my concrete questions are:

# Should we always discriminate between the ''introduction to the BB'' and the BB proper every time the introduction is cited?
# Should we always explain that the introduction is "controversial" when the BB introduction is used as a source?
# Should we always describe the controversy around the figures presented in the introduction when the introduction is being used as the source for these figures?
# Should we explain the objections to the "generic Communism" concept every time the combined "Communist death toll" calculated in the BB introduction is being discussed in an article?
These questions are independent, and the answers can be, for example, "Yes - No - No - Yes".

:--[[User:Paul Siebert|Paul Siebert]] ([[User talk:Paul Siebert|talk]]) 05:41, 5 June 2018 (UTC)}}


=== [[Talk:Mass killings under Communist regimes#rfc_A7D01DC|Talk:Mass killings under Communist regimes]] expired 2018-06-30 01:01 ===
* Id: A7D01DC

* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The current topic  "''Mass killing under Communist regimes''" has several possible interpretations. 
Would ''"Non-combatant deaths attributed to communist regimes"''  reasonably reduce the number of interpretations? This would eliminate arguments as to causality, and intent, being critical to the general topic, as well as arguments as to the definition of "Communist" as a proper adjective. 00:21, 31 May 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Liberty University#rfc_18CAE7C|Talk:Liberty University]] expired 2018-07-01 01:01 ===

{{rfcquote|text=
This text is currently under dispute, with some editors arguing that it does not belong on Liberty University's Wikipedia page or that it should be trimmed (the formatting for the following three sources in the first sentence got screwed up[https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2016/10/trump-evangelical-falwell-liberty-university-christian-conservatives-214394][https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2017/08/25/jerry-falwell-miami-hostel-liberty-university-trey-falwell-215528][https://www.insidehighered.com/news/2017/11/01/jerry-falwell-jr-relishes-new-fight-donald-trump-liberty-university-peaks]):

* ''In 2016, a student editor said that an opinion column critical of presidential candidate Donald Trump was censored by LU's president Jerry Falwell Jr.<ref name=":7">{{Cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/story/2016/10/jerry-falwell-donald-trump-liberty-229964|title=Falwell censored anti-Trump column, Liberty U student  editor says|work=POLITICO|access-date=2018-04-24}}</ref><ref name=":3">{{Cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2016/10/trump-evangelical-falwell-liberty-university-christian-conservatives-214394|title=How Trump Is Dividing Jerry Falwell’s University|work=POLITICO Magazine|access-date=2018-04-24}}</ref><ref name=":6">{{Cite news|url=https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2017/08/25/jerry-falwell-miami-hostel-liberty-university-trey-falwell-215528|title=My Weekend at the Falwells’ South Beach Flophouse|work=POLITICO Magazine|access-date=2018-04-24}}</ref><ref name=":4">{{Cite news|url=https://www.insidehighered.com/news/2017/11/01/jerry-falwell-jr-relishes-new-fight-donald-trump-liberty-university-peaks|title=Jerry Falwell Jr. relishes new fight for Donald Trump as Liberty University peaks|access-date=2018-04-24|language=en}}</ref> The column was written after a video was released showing Trump boasting about sexually assaulting women.<ref name=":7" /> Trump's candidacy caused fractures at the university, as a number of students disagreed with Trump, protested the university's ties with Trump, and were critical of Falwell Jr.'s staunch support of Trump.<ref name=":3" /><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/grade-point/wp/2016/10/12/liberty-is-not-trump-u-students-protest-donald-trump/|title=Liberty University students protest association with Trump|last=Shapiro|first=T. Rees|date=2016-10-13|work=Washington Post|access-date=2018-04-24|last2=Bailey|first2=Sarah Pulliam|language=en-US|issn=0190-8286|last3=Svrluga|first3=Susan|last4=Clement|first4=Scott}}</ref> Mark DeMoss, chief of staff of Falwell Sr., was forced to resign from Liberty’s board of trustees after criticizing the university's close affiliation with Trump.<ref name=":8">{{Cite news|url=https://www.vox.com/identities/2017/11/4/16597988/liberty-university-anti-trump-author-falwell-jonathan-martin-evangelical|title=Liberty University booted an anti-Trump Christian author from campus|work=Vox|access-date=2018-04-24}}</ref> Liberty University rescinded a speaking invitation of Jonathan Merritt, an alumnus of the school, after he criticized Liberty University, and expelled Christian author Jonathan Martin from campus due to his repeated criticisms of the university's affiliation with Trump.<ref name=":8" /><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2017/11/why-liberty-university-banned-an-anti-trump-christian-author-from-campus/544571/|title=Why Liberty University Kicked an Anti-Trump Christian Author Off Campus|last=Merritt|first=Jonathan|work=The Atlantic|access-date=2018-04-24|language=en-US}}</ref>''

* ''Some students protested again when President Trump equated white supremacists with counter-protesters at a white supremacist march in Charlotesville, Virginia.<ref name=":9">{{Cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/morning-mix/wp/2017/08/21/liberty-university-graduates-return-diplomas-because-of-support-for-trump-by-jerry-falwell-jr/|title=Jerry Falwell Jr. keeps defending Trump as Liberty University grads return diplomas|last=Schmidt|first=Samantha|date=2017-08-21|work=Washington Post|access-date=2018-04-24|last2=Wang|first2=Amy B.|language=en-US|issn=0190-8286}}</ref> After Trump's remarks, Liberty University president Falwell Jr. said that he was “so proud” of Trump for his “bold truthful” statement on the tragedy.<ref name=":9" /> A number of students returned their diplomas to Liberty University and called on the university to disavow Trump's remarks.<ref name=":9" /><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.npr.org/2017/08/20/544776964/some-liberty-university-grads-are-returning-their-diplomas-to-protest-trump|title=Some Liberty University Grads Are Returning Their Diplomas To Protest Trump|work=NPR.org|access-date=2018-04-24|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/08/21/us/jerry-falwell-liberty-university-trump.html|title=Liberty University Alumni Return Diplomas in Protest of Trump Remarks|date=2017-08-21|work=The New York Times|access-date=2018-04-24|language=en-US|issn=0362-4331}}</ref> The students argued that Trump's remarks were "incompatible with Liberty University’s stated values, and incompatible with a Christian witness."<ref name=":9" />''

Does this belong? If something should be trimmed, what precisely should be trimmed? Note that the content is extremely well-sourced, covers a number of notable events (student protests, senior staff resigning, speakers being disinvited) and covers events that are of obvious importance to a university that plays a prominent role in Republican politics. Consider for example if LU was "fractured" in the early 2000s over the university's relationship to George W. Bush (or Ronald Reagan in the 80s) during his presidency with prominent student protests, students returning diplomas, senior staff resigning and alumni speakers being disinvited, and that all of this was reported by 9 reliable sources. Would anyone seriously argue that such content would not have encyclopedic value (an interesting notable episode in the history of this university) and easily fulfill Wiki policy requirements? [[User:Snooganssnoogans|Snooganssnoogans]] ([[User talk:Snooganssnoogans|talk]]) 00:51, 1 June 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Did you know#rfc_0E23E3F|Wikipedia talk:Did you know]] expired 2018-07-02 07:01 ===
* Id: 0E23E3F
* User: Yoninah
* Date: 2018-06-11 14:44:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|845609269|POLICY 845609269}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|848489771|POLICY 848489771}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
[[WP:ERRORS#DYK current|A discussion <del>is going on</del> <ins>was previously</ins> at ERRORS]] ([[Special:Permalink/845492490#DYK current|permalink to final version]]) about whether hooks reporting murders, riots, etc., should be featured on the main page. The hook in question, which was pulled, was:
*... that a newlywed man was killed and his wife seriously injured in February after opening a '''[[Patnagarh bombing|parcel bomb]]''' that looked like a wedding gift?
* We need to build consensus on this point, rather than have administrators feel free to pull hooks they don't like. Please add your comments here. Thank you, [[User:Yoninah|Yoninah]] ([[User talk:Yoninah|talk]]) 14:44, 11 June 2018 (UTC)}}

Two sources state that Kolis (the first people in Mumbai) originated and migrated from Gujarat.<ref name=munshi1>{{cite book|url=https://archive.org/stream/in.ernet.dli.2015.97812/2015.97812.Gujarat-And-Its-Literature-1852#page/n31/mode/2up/search/Kolis|quote=The next immigrants into the islands of Bombay were the Kolis, who on all authorities continued to be their original inhabitants till Aungier founded the city of Bombay. Kathiawad and Central Gujarāt was the home of the Kolis in pre-historic times.|title=Gujarāt and its literature, from early times to 1852|first=Kanaiyalal M.|last=Munshi|publisher=[[Bharatiya Vidya Bhavan Educational Trust|Bharatiya Vidya Bhavan]]|page=xix|year=1954}}</ref><ref name=oriental1>{{cite journal|title=Journal of the Oriental Institute|volume=33|first1=M. D.|last1=David|quote=The kolis who suceeded the stone-age men on the island brought with them from Gujarat their patron goddess Mummai whom their descendants still worship in Kathiawar. The name of Bombay is derived from this koli goddess.|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=quINAAAAYAAJ&focus=searchwithinvolume&q=koli+goddess|publisher=Oriental Institute|year=1983}}</ref> One of these sources also mentions that the name Mumbai is derived from the Koli goddess Mummai who also originated in Gujarat.<ref name=oriental1></ref> Should we add this information to the article? === [[Talk:University of London#rfc_EC398BE|Talk:University of London]] expired 2018-07-02 22:01 ===
* Id: EC398BE
* User: Aloneinthewild
* Date: 2018-06-02 21:18:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|844142001|SOC 844142001}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|848584758|SOC 848584758}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This is not usually an area I would stand my ground over but I feel I really can't edit this article without being in a revert cycle. This is part of a wider issue on this article with behaviour verging on ownership and minor attacks in edit summaries towards multiple users- labelling them and their edits 'vandalism', 'Bias or personal opinions', 'biased and not educated' and the best one 'Wikipedia should not suffer for your trash.' (see the recent [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_London&action=history history]). 

All the conflicting edits appear to involve IPs addresses in a similar locality. Previously conflicts (over different content) involved a failure to engage the editor in the talk discussion (see [[#Popular culture]], hence I turn to an Rfc this time.

The content under debate is the lead sentence, should it read:
*{{tq|The '''University of London''' (informally '''London University''' and commonly abbreviated as '''Lond. or, more rarely, Londin''')}} or
*{{tq|The '''University of London''' (abbreviated as '''Lond.''' or more rarely '''Londin''' in [[Post-nominal letters|post-nominals]]) }}
I believe the second option is more appropriate, firstly, I see no sources showing it is referred to as '''London University'''. Even so, its unnecessary to tell people that the order of the name can be rearranged and guess what - same place. Second, its name is not ''commonly'' abbreviated as these abbreviations. To say so is misleading, it is only abbreviated like this for [[Post-nominal letters]]. This is why I also favour simply keeping to the sentence that is already at the end of the lead (in my first edit that as reverted). 

Thanks for reading this far, hopefully some extra input can help we can avoid these endless contact disputes
--[[User:Aloneinthewild|Aloneinthewild]] ([[User talk:Aloneinthewild|talk]]) 21:18, 2 June 2018 (UTC)}}
